Current Affairs Commentary

Children's Year and Children's Literature 15

— Bing

Children's literature is often called "food for the spirit of children." This is a very appropriate name and the words used are very precise. The so-called "food" includes delicacies and flavors that are not easily accessible to ordinary people, and even if consumed, may not necessarily be nutritious. By using the term "food," we exclude such things and focus specifically on grains. Grains are essential for life, and are indispensable to people of all social classes. To use this as a metaphor for children's literature is even more appropriate. Even if parents do not buy all kinds of reading material for their children, even the most remote rural schools will contain traces of children's literature. Children sing and play outside of school, and inside they unroll books to read and enjoy. Their wisdom is developed and their character is shaped. Children's literature is truly "food" for children, not comparable to candy, fresh oranges, and water.

Children's Year began this month. Publishers are joining this grand event and are publishing advertisements to inexpensively issue children's literature so that children can benefit and improve their spiritual health. This intention is beautiful and commendable. Looking at the catalogs of children's literature from various publishers, there are collections like forests, with hundreds of volumes. Children looking at them can choose what they love and enjoy them greatly. Those who wish for a good future for children can also feel gratified.

However, after careful examination of the substance of the children's literature from various publishers, those who feel gratified will soon feel disappointed. This is because what they find is that this "food" may not be nutritious. The growth of grains depends on the hidden potential of nature, but even with human intervention, there are differences in quality. This so-called "food for the spirit" has its growth independent of other forces, and its quality depends entirely on the diligence of cultivation. Careless cultivation will result in mediocre results. I have often looked at the children's literature from various publishers and summarized several shortcomings: emperors and princesses appear at the drop of a hat; gods, immortals, ghosts, and strange boxes are everywhere. Cunning schemes and deception are falsely called wisdom. Performing a small good deed leads to wealth and nobility. Weakness is seen as a virtue and physical labor is seen as hard work. All of these things are inappropriate for the current era, especially for the children of our nation today. Unfortunately, we often encounter these things in children's literature. This is the fault of impure consciousness. The layout is simple and clumsy, and you can guess the ending from the beginning. The language is empty and vague, and you don't retain any impression even after finishing the volume. Children love activity, like change, and hate empty talk. They want to see real things. Children's literature is not enough to satisfy their wishes, so they turn to other things. The picture books lined up in the streets and alleys, which education experts see as poison, become treasures for children. This is the fault of unskilled technique. The language used either violates logic or deviates from grammar. Sometimes they mix in rural slang that people from other places cannot understand, or they simply believe in imitating sentences that our people are not accustomed to. They casually claim to imitate the tone of children, but in reality children would never speak like that. Children will get used to it over time, and their language and thinking will go astray. Not only will language teaching encounter obstacles, but teaching in other subjects will also be affected. This is the fault of inappropriate language. Their poems are also often objectionable. Often there is no poetic interest and no impression. Their songs for physical exercises say "Get up early, learn exercises, be healthy, have high aspirations." Songs about scenery say "Red flowers bloom, butterflies come, beautiful scenery, truly lovely." Or they pile up admonitory texts like a strict father scolding his son, or they mix in everyday language like a beach song on stage. They seek only to rhyme and do not care about awkward sentences. The meaning is between understandable and incomprehensible, and the flavor is between existing and non-existing. The feelings they give will make children suddenly realize that poetry is such a boring and tedious thing. Even if they never develop an interest in it in their entire lives, there is nothing to regret. Therefore, children's poetry is not only insufficient to cultivate character, but is even a tool to block intelligence. As for their drawings, they are even less collaborative. Often they only have outlines, and they lack any wonderful details. Not to mention anything else, just speaking of the characters, the outlines do not correspond to anatomy, and the expressions are all stiff. The children all look dull, and the workers and farmers all become ruffians. Children love to look at drawings. When a book arrives, this is the first thing they do. If they cannot find good works, they will also enjoy the inferior ones. However, their ability to perceive and depict things is being suppressed. The lack of achievements in drawing education has many reasons, but it is not due to the crudeness of illustrations in children's literature. The above are some of the major issues. If you want to describe them in detail, even 100,000 words may not be enough. I don't mean to be hypercritical, but the facts are as they are. What's the point of covering them up? The world is not lacking in wise parents, good teachers, and enlightened educators. If you ask them about children's literature, they will definitely say that my views are incomplete and my words are not exhaustive.

This raises two questions. Is the spiritual food that is piled up in warehouses just a facade with a completely different quality? Generally speaking, we can be proud of its abundance. Strictly speaking, isn't it almost equal to zero? Now, during Children's Year, the spiritual food of children is almost equal to zero. Those who can feel disappointed will go one step further to think about it. Because this spiritual food, which is just a facade, is displayed around children every day, allowing them to take it and swallow it at any time, how much does it harm the nutrition of children? How much does it hinder the vitality of children? Even if you have clever calculations, you probably can't answer it quickly. Now, during Children's Year, children are swallowing spiritual food of completely different quality to hinder their vitality. Isn't this even more disappointing?

The occurrence and existence of anything cannot be separated from the relationship of time and space. Today, our nation has children's literature that is just a facade with a completely different quality. There are various reasons for this, but writers and publishers take it too lightly and make it too easy. They cannot escape their responsibility. Children's literature is of course a commodity. However, even ordinary commodities must be suitable for the purchaser. Moreover, children's literature is food for the spirit of children. How can it be hastily produced so that "no one recognizes the goods once they leave the door"? It is not easier to teach in a university than to teach in elementary school. You can know that writing children's literature is not easier than writing works that will be passed down for generations. Unfortunately, this basic concept is ignored by writers and publishers. They only seek to produce more and make goods faster, which makes the colorful and dazzling things displayed in the bookshelves are actually the same as nothing. It is even worse to see it as harmful. It is truly regrettable.

It is useless to only sigh and spoil the fun. I hope that writers and publishers will wake up now and establish a basic concept first. Children's literature must be produced with caution. All the above-mentioned shortcomings must be avoided. Don't boast about the fact that you have piles of things from the past. You should examine them one by one with a calm mind. Quickly eliminate the worst ones and retain the better ones. On the one hand, start from scratch and create good works. This is of course not something that can be done in a hurry. In the future, when there are more good works, then even the better ones will be eliminated. Perhaps children will have spiritual food of pure quality, and their character and wisdom can get adequate nutrition. Are the enlightened writers and publishers interested in this? Starting from Children's Year, thoroughly improving children's literature is also a major step for children.

Chen Shuren Resigns as Chairman of the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission 19

(Nanjing) Chen Shuren submitted his resignation as Chairman of the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission to Premier Kong on the 9th. His original petition stated: "I, Shuren, with my limited talent, have mistakenly been entrusted with a heavy responsibility, serving in overseas Chinese affairs for three years. At a time of national difficulty, measures are even more hindered. Looking back on my tenure, not only has the welfare of overseas Chinese not seen any improvement, but even their suffering has not been alleviated in the slightest. Asking myself, I am filled with anxiety. Rather than causing further delay, it is better to retire early. Therefore, I sincerely request permission to resign from the position of Chairman of the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission and appoint another capable person to quickly take over. I also earnestly request that this be forwarded and await orders with trepidation." (10th Central News Agency Dispatch)

Liu Guitang's Bandit Gang Returns to Xinglong 20

(Tianjin) Liu Guitang's bandit gang planned to harass the Zunhua-Malan Valley area, but on the 9th, they were intercepted by our troops. Failing in their attempt, the bandits fled back to the Daodaoshui and Xiaodaoshui areas of Xinglong, looting all the villages there. Even the poorest households were stripped of everything they owned and meticulously recorded before they were taken away. (10th Daily Dispatch)

(Beiping) The bandit gang discovered west of Yuguan, in the Shihe area, is a combined force of remnants from Qi Wenping and Liu Guitang. After being encircled and suppressed by Zhang Yantian's special police force in the war zone, the bandits were unable to withstand the pressure and began to flee out of the Great Wall line via Yiyuankou on the 7th of this month. Unexpectedly, about a hundred remnants of the bandit gang attempted to sneak back into the interior on the night of the 8th. Fortunately, the police and militia stationed at Yiyuankou were prepared and launched a fierce counterattack and encirclement. After a fierce battle lasting about two hours, the bandits suffered heavy casualties. Only about thirty people remained and fled into the territory of Rehe. (10th Daily Dispatch)

Liu Zuozhou's Coffin Shipped to Shenyang 21

(Beiping) Wang Xiacai, secretary of the Luan-Yu District Office, arrived in Beiping this morning after being summoned by Yin Rugeng, to report on the situation in Tangshan-Luanxian. He is scheduled to return to Tangshan tonight. (10th Daily Dispatch)

(Tianjin) Liu Zuozhou's body was placed in a coffin on the 6th. The coffin was made of foreign tile and contained alcohol for preservation. A grand memorial service was held on the 8th, after which the coffin was moved to the station. On the 9th, it was transported on a flatcar attached to the Ping-Shenyang train, bound for his ancestral home in Shenyang. In addition to the 2,000 yuan allocated by the provincial government, merchants and residents of Luanxian also voluntarily donated 1,000 yuan for funeral expenses. (10th Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Nanjing) Chairman Shang Zhen of the Hebei Provincial Government telegraphed the Executive Yuan, reporting on the handling of the Liu Zuozhou case and requesting instructions on all matters. (10th Daily Dispatch)

(Beiping) News of the resolution of the Luanxian case, as reported in Nanjing, is unknown to both Chinese and Japanese officials here. (10th Reuters Dispatch)

Jones' Detention in Rehe Province; No News of Escape 23

(Beiping) Since British reporter Jones was abducted to a certain location in Fengning County, Rehe Province, negotiations between the responsible officials sent by the Chahar Provincial Government and the bandits have stalled due to the inability to cross the border, causing the rescue efforts to come to a standstill. Military Attaché Scator of the British Embassy in Beiping subsequently contacted Military Attaché Takahashi of the Japanese Embassy, who telegraphed Chengde to inquire about the truth. Last night, a reply confirmed that Jones was indeed in Rehe Province. Following the British request, Takahashi telegraphed Chengde that night, requesting an urgent rescue of Jones and escort to Beiping. As of tonight, Takahashi has not yet received a telegram confirming Jones' escape. It is generally believed that Jones will be able to escape from the bandit den within a few days. (10th Daily Dispatch)

(Beiping) According to today's news, there are currently five groups of negotiators approaching the bandits separately, hoping that Jones can be released as soon as possible. Three of these groups were dispatched by the Chahar Provincial Government. Their efforts are expected to yield concrete results soon. According to a Japanese spokesperson, various parties in Rehe are looking for opportunities to rescue Jones and plan to pay the ransom first. The exact amount demanded by the bandits has not been determined, but the latest information indicates it is 90,000 yuan. It is reported that Jones was detained in the area where the Sino-Japanese conflict occurred in mid-January of this year. Although the conflict has been resolved, the border has not been clearly demarcated, which explains why the telegram from Zhangjiakou indicated that Jones was in Chahar Province, while the telegram from Chengde stated that he had entered Rehe Province, causing conflicting information. (10th Reuters Dispatch)

(Beiping) It was once rumored that British reporter Jones had been released, but according to a reply telegram from Chengde received by Japanese Embassy Military Attaché Takahashi on the evening of the 9th, Jones was confirmed to be still in Rehe Province. Following the British request, Takahashi telegraphed Chengde that night, requesting an urgent rescue. Since Jones was abducted to Rehe Province, our rescue efforts have been quite difficult, and we are now seeking other methods to vigorously proceed. British Embassy Military Attaché Miller is still staying in Zhangjiakou, working with the Chahar Provincial Government to handle all matters. (10th Central News Agency Dispatch)

Long-Distance Bus Robbed Between Beiping and Tianjin; Incident Occurs in Nan Yulinzhuang; Fifteen Passengers Kidnapped 24

(Beiping) Eight long-distance buses traveling from Tianjin to Beiping were robbed yesterday afternoon. When the seventh bus passed through Nan Yulinzhuang near Tongxian, more than 30 bandits suddenly emerged from the sorghum fields, firing two shots and surrounding the bus. All the valuables in the bus were looted, and fifteen passengers were kidnapped. The bus has been released. This morning, extensive inquiries were made about the bandits' whereabouts, but their escape route remains unknown. (10th Daily Dispatch)

It is also reported that the Japanese side has raised the issue of the Cangzhou-Shijiazhuang Railway. It is said that the Japanese side has decided to establish the North China Cotton Association first among the various companies developing North China industries. The association's headquarters will be located in Tangshan or Tianjin and will serve as a guiding and controlling body for the cotton industry in North China. (10th Daily Dispatch)

(Nanjing) The Executive Yuan held a review meeting on the 10th to discuss the draft Civil Servants Savings Regulations. The draft consists of 14 articles in total and stipulates that those with monthly salaries below 100 yuan will save 2% of their salary each month, while those with salaries above 600 yuan will save 10%. The review has been completed and will be submitted to the Executive Yuan for a decision. (10th Daily Dispatch)

Page 8

British Government Economic Advisor Discusses Mission to China Before Departure; Stabilizing Finance and Promoting Trade; Hopes to Meet with American Representatives in Shanghai 41

(London) Sir Otto Niemeyer, chief economic advisor to the British government, departed today with Mr. Paton of the Treasury and Mr. Rogers, an expert from the Bank of England, aboard the Empress of Britain for China. Before his departure, Sir Otto met with a Reuters reporter, declining to discuss the details of his mission to China. He stated that his primary objective was to investigate the current situation and report back to the government. He added that the government's decision to send him to China reflects the government's concern for China's financial and economic difficulties. The purpose of this trip is to determine whether cooperation with other relevant countries can produce recommendations to help China restore a stable and satisfactory situation, which will benefit China's export trade and foreign trade. He will take a broad view of the situation in the Far East and meet with Chinese authorities. He will, of course, adopt their views as much as possible. Sir Otto also hopes to make contact with important figures in the British business community in Shanghai, stating that he has already met with their representatives in London. Sir Otto denied rumors that he would go to Washington but said that he hopes to meet with several American representatives in Shanghai to cooperate. Sir Otto will spend two days in Toronto visiting relatives when he arrives in Canada and will stay in Tokyo for several days when he passes through Japan to meet with Japanese officials. (10th Reuters Dispatch)

Rumors About Sir Otto's Visit to China Are Unreliable; US Silver Purchases Have Decreased Significantly 42

(London) According to responsible sources, the mission of British financial representative Sir Otto Niemeyer's visit to China is solely to investigate China's monetary and economic situation and British investment interests in China. Various rumors that Britain and Japan are planning to divide the Chinese market, or that Sir Otto's visit to China has other missions, such as studying naval issues in preparation for convening a 1936 naval conference, are all inaccurate. Responsible sources also believe that Sir Otto's visit to Japan before going to China is intended to express Britain's hope that Japan will no longer oppose the dispatch of financial representatives to China by various countries. Initially, Britain proposed that representatives from Britain, the United States, France, Japan, or Italy go to Nanjing to hold a Chinese monetary conference, but it was abandoned due to Japan's firm opposition. Later, the method was changed, with each country sending financial representatives to China separately to submit reports to their respective governments, avoiding the form of a conference. Therefore, the British government appointed its chief treasury advisor, Sir Otto Niemeyer, and the French government appointed Mr. Renault-Sios, financial vice-counselor at its embassy in London, to visit China in the near future. However, the American financial representative has not yet been appointed. The mission of the British financial representative is to investigate China's financial situation, especially the monetary situation, to place Chinese currency on a stable foundation, but its importance is not limited to this. Many British investments in railways in China have failed to repay their debts on time. Studying the current situation of these railways is also one of Sir Otto Niemeyer's main missions. (9th Havas Dispatch)

(London) Responsible sources believe that the British government's dispatch of financial representative Sir Otto Niemeyer to China for investigation has two main missions: one is to stabilize China's currency, and the other is to enable the Nanjing government to obtain international loans guaranteed by foreign governments, thereby strengthening the position of the Chinese government. Regarding the first mission, responsible sources believe that the Chinese currency can be linked to the pound sterling. However, setting a fixed exchange rate between the Chinese currency and the pound sterling would not only require excessive funds to protect this exchange rate but would also endanger the gold bloc, making it difficult to achieve. In addition, it seems possible to imitate the Argentine "Peso" method, using the pound sterling as a measure of the rise and fall of the Chinese currency, that is, as the "benchmark" of the Chinese currency. If so, it would be feasible. Financial figures here also believe that only with the economic recovery of China can Chinese railway loans be restored to repay principal and interest. It would be a mistake to lend money to China to repay the arrears owed to Chinese railway loan bondholders. This is why Britain advocates international loans to China for construction expenses. However, these two plans inevitably face various difficulties. One is the opposition of the Japanese government, which Sir Otto will try to overcome by persuading the Japanese government to understand that Britain's plan has no political background and that its purpose is only to improve China's commercial and financial position, from which Japan's trade with China will benefit first and foremost. The second is the difficulty of the monetary problem, which Sir Otto will solve using the above-mentioned method. The third is that if international loans are guaranteed by foreign governments, the parliaments of various countries may not be able to approve them, as most countries are currently suffering from excessive budget burdens and cannot bear this burden. Therefore, the purpose of the relevant governments sending representatives to China separately is to investigate China's current situation and its economic improvement, draft reports, and submit them to their respective governments so that the governments can propose legislation to their parliaments based on the reasons stated in the reports, requesting guarantees for Chinese loans, which would then be more likely to be approved by the parliaments. (10th Havas Dispatch)

(Washington) It was learned today from reliable sources here that the silver purchase plan will make it impossible for the United States to cooperate with Britain in sending a financial mission to China, and even informal consultations are not possible. This is because Sir Otto Niemeyer, the British government's chief economic advisor, is traveling to the Far East from London via Canada and is not going through the United States. On the eve of Sir Otto's departure, officials stated that there was no progress on this matter here. Responsible sources here also said that the US government still adheres to the policy of collective action to help China's economic prosperity, but it must continue to purchase silver based on congressional mandates. This makes it difficult for the United States to cooperate with Sir Otto, as the government fears that joining the cooperation will conflict with the congressional silver purchase law and put it in a difficult position. It is not yet known what attitude the United States will take towards China. For the time being, it will likely remain in a state of aloofness. (9th Kuomintang News Agency Dispatch)

(Washington) It was learned today that a total of 3,180,503 yuan worth of silver was imported in the week ending August 2, the lowest number since June 21. The small amount of silver imported has led experts to believe that the United States has stopped buying silver and that silver prices will stabilize. Of the silver imported this time, 2,670,970 yuan came from Mexico, 551,695 yuan came from Canada, and Britain supplied only 31,000 yuan. The imported gold was worth a total of 7,884,950 yuan. (9th Kuomintang News Agency Dispatch)

(Washington) The silver imported into the United States in the week ending August 2 decreased significantly compared to the previous week, by approximately 3,079,000 yuan. The total value of silver imported this week was 3,181,000 yuan, of which Britain accounted for 32,000 yuan, Mexico 2,068,000 yuan, Canada 552,000 yuan, Peru 401,000 yuan, Chile 57,000 yuan, the Philippines 5,000 yuan, Honduras 54,000 yuan, Guatemala 1,000 yuan, Cuba 5,000 yuan, and Ecuador 5,000 yuan. (9th Reuters Dispatch)

(London) During the week ending August 7, there was little change in the import and export of silver in the United Kingdom. Exports totaled 774,000 pounds, of which purchases by the United States accounted for 759,000 pounds. In the previous week, exports totaled 768,000 pounds, of which shipments to the United States accounted for 735,000 pounds. Imports of silver during the week ending August 7 totaled 127,000 pounds, of which 33,000 pounds came from Soviet Russia and 45,000 pounds came from India. In the previous week, imports totaled 505,000 pounds, of which 72,000 pounds came from Soviet Russia, 285,000 pounds came from Japan, 25,000 pounds came from France, and 29,000 pounds came from Iraq. This week's net exports were 647,000 pounds, an increase of 381,000 pounds compared to the previous week's surplus of 266,000 pounds. (9th Reuters Dispatch)

Montreal According to a report from the Dominion Bureau of Statistics, Canada's silver production in the past few months reached 6,168,025 ounces, a decrease of 5.80% compared to the same period last year. (9th Kuomintang News Agency Dispatch)

Sao Paulo Mr. Kellogg, who initiated the famous peace pact, told a Reuters interviewer today that neither Italy nor Ethiopia has any reason to resort to war to resolve their affairs. Any country in the world has the right to demand that other signatory countries uphold and support this pact. (Reuters, 9th)

Bellingzona, Switzerland Although Rome denies reports of Italian soldiers deserting due to fear of the expedition, it is widely believed that a large number of Italian soldiers have escaped into Ticino, the Italian-speaking region of Switzerland, in the past few days. Many of them were ordered to go to Northeast Africa. Italian border guards are now closely monitoring the border to prevent Italian soldiers from continuing to escape into Switzerland. Therefore, deserters have to cross the border into Switzerland through the deserted and uninhabited mountains. Once they arrive in Ticino, it is not difficult for them to blend in, as the residents of the region speak Italian and are mostly sympathetic to the deserters. Meanwhile, according to a Reuters dispatch from the Swiss capital, the Swiss Federal Council attaches great importance to a certain propaganda campaign currently underway in Ticino, advocating the annexation of the region into Italy, and has decided to charge one man and one woman arrested in Bellingzona with high treason and punish them according to law. All employees of Ticino who participate in the propaganda movement will be investigated. (Reuters, 10th)

Addis Ababa According to news from here today, if war breaks out, the Ethiopian King will confront the Italian army on the battlefield with seven armies of approximately 660,000 men. 250,000 of these men will be supplied with rifles by the government, while the rest will purchase their own weapons. The armies in the southeast, northwest, and south will be led by their respective princes, while the central army will maintain rear security and prepare to assist wherever needed most urgently. Each of the seven armies has fifty battalions, with each battalion consisting of three thousand men. Ethiopia has approximately 300,000 to 1,000,000 rifles and approximately 200 cannons, but their effectiveness is doubtful, as some of them are up to seventy years old. There are approximately 400 machine guns, and a similar number of quick-firing rifles. There are eight aircraft, but only six are able to take off. The Ethiopian military will adopt guerrilla warfare tactics. Therefore, the military authorities do not value modern weaponry, except for rifles and machine guns. The Ethiopian government is quite concerned about the lack of military supplies in Ethiopia, but hopes that Ethiopian soldiers can compensate for their lack of modern weaponry and organization with their endurance, courage, patriotism, and vitality. (Reuters, 10th)

(Paris) The Ethiopian Minister to France, Haile Woldie, stated in an interview published in Quotidien today that "to seek peace, one must be armed" remains an irrefutable truth. Therefore, Ethiopia's purchase of weapons from abroad is a result of circumstances. It is unfair for all countries to prohibit the import of weapons into Ethiopia, as this action only harms Ethiopia, while Italy, which has the ability to manufacture its own weapons, suffers no loss. According to the Ethiopian Minister, people from various countries have come to offer their services to the Ethiopian army in droves, but as the Ethiopian government has not yet issued instructions on this matter, it can only reject them. The Minister also stated that Belgian military instructors have been working in Ethiopia for many years. As for whether other foreign military experts are needed, the government has not yet made any indication of this. Finally, Haile Woldie stated that Ethiopia's trust in the work of the arbitration committee remains unshaken and that it also has admiration for the League of Nations. However, when all else fails, Ethiopians will defend their motherland, with or without weapons. (National Telegram, 10th)

In addition to England and Germany, a large number of military personnel from Poland, Sweden, Czechoslovakia, and other countries have volunteered. Even from the Gold Coast, one person is willing to supply 10,000 soldiers to serve Ethiopia, but they have all been politely declined. (Reuters, 10th)

(Paris) People gather in front of the Ethiopian Embassy here every day to petition to join the Ethiopian army, but embassy staff have refused their requests. According to the Ethiopian ambassador today, he has not received instructions from his country and is therefore unable to accept such petitions at this time. (Reuters, 10th)

(Paris) The "Paris Echo" correspondent in London discusses the reasons for Germany's conservative silence on the Italo-Ethiopian issue, stating that Germany has not expressed an attitude towards the development of the East African issue, apparently waiting for an opportunity to take action. Well-informed sources know that when former British Foreign Secretary Simon and Lord Privy Seal Eden visited Berlin this spring, the German government raised the issue of colonies. In this case, Germany will sooner or later raise demands for colonies. Germany will either demand the redistribution of colonies or demand that the major powers distribute the world's major industrial raw materials so that Germany can also get a piece of the pie. The presentation of this demand is only a matter of time and will ultimately be unavoidable. (Havas, 10th)

Representatives from Thirty-Seven Countries Attend World Physiology Congress in Leningrad, 1,500 Representatives Attend, Russian Representative Describes the Status of Soviet Culture 49

Leningrad The 15th International Physiological Congress opened here recently. 1,500 representatives attended, including 900 foreign physiologists representing 37 countries. The congress was chaired by Pavlov, the famous Soviet biologist, who delivered the opening speech. (Havas, 9th)

(Moscow) The 15th World Physiological Congress opened in Leningrad on the 9th, with 1,500 representatives attending, as well as members and guests of the Soviet government. The opening speech was delivered by researcher Pavlov, followed by congratulatory speeches from government representatives Uglov, Secretary of the Central Executive Committee of the Soviet Union, Karpinsky, President of the Academy of Sciences, and Kodatsky, Chairman of the Leningrad Soviet. In his speech, Pavlov emphasized the importance of the congress for educating new scientists and said that the Soviet government is very concerned about scientific work and young people who love science, and has allocated huge sums of money to assist them. Pavlov mentioned the war crisis, saying that it is a "cruel way to solve life's difficulties," and said, "Our powerful motherland is fighting for peace and never covets an inch of other people's land, which is very gratifying." At that time, the audience cheered loudly. Pavlov finally expressed his gratitude to the Soviet government for its assistance in the success of the congress. Subsequently, Ukolov, on behalf of the Soviet government, said that it was very gratifying that the congress could be held in the Soviet Union, because in the Soviet Union, physiology is progressing rapidly because the government pays close attention to scientific work, and the number of physiologists is in the thousands, no longer calculated by individuals. Amidst applause, Ukolov went on to recount Pavlov's great contributions to the development of Soviet physiology, and how the government and people admire Pavlov's work. "The Soviet working masses, with the help of scientific power, have completely transformed an illiterate country. Today, 500,000 young people in the Soviet Union are studying at universities, and there are more than 1,000 scientific research institutes and 41,000 scientific workers. The Soviet Union has become an advanced industrial country, with electrical stations all over the country. Its metal industry and machinery manufacturing production already account for the first place in Europe and the second place in the world. Its agricultural mechanization is the most extensive in the world. This great work is the realization of the immortal teachings of our mentor Lenin, and all of it is carried out under the leadership of his outstanding disciple Stalin." At that time, there was a loud burst of applause, lasting for quite some time. "All the victories of our country's science and technology are in raising the cultural level of the masses and maintaining international peace," Ukolov concluded, "The Soviet government hopes that this congress of the world's largest scientists will promote the development of physiology and benefit the working masses." Finally, Ukolov wished the representatives of the congress success in their work. After congratulatory speeches by Karpinsky and Kodatsky, Chairman of the Leningrad Soviet, the congress listened to a report by Professor Cannon, the American representative. The congress elected Pavlov, Professor Lapicque (France), and Hill (England) as members of the presidium. (TASS, 10th)

Laval Addresses Provincial Governors on the Implementation of Emergency Decrees, Strike Waves in Various Places are Quiet 50

(Havas, 9th)

(Paris) In the past few days, there have been strikes in Brest, Toulon, and Le Havre to protest against the 10% wage cut. Today, all three places passed quietly. Strikers in Toulon had a fierce fight with the police yesterday. Countless shop windows were smashed, resulting in two deaths and three injuries. Forty-four people were arrested. The shops are still closed, proving the severity of the riots. After the Champoillon set sail, the Columbia continued to raise anchor and set sail for the Baltic Sea. The Lafayette also set sail for Canada with 320 French veterans. The governors of all departments are now gathered in Paris to listen to Prime Minister Laval explain the new economic laws aimed at protecting the franc and restoring the country's economy. This is truly an unprecedented event in the history of the Third Republic of France, but two prefects, due to strikes in Toulon and Brest, were unable to be present. (Reuters, 9th)

(Paris) Order has been restored in all French seaports today. Workers in the ports of Brest and Toulon have also gone to work in local shipyards and arsenals. Officials are closely examining the background of the revolutionary activities. The same is true for those arrested in the port of Toulon. Armed soldiers still guard the stations. Many people who have observed the scene of the incident are convinced that these disturbances cannot be regarded as a political demonstration. Socialist and Communist newspapers have condemned the right wing for inciting the riots, believing that the government has laid the groundwork for blatant intervention. Left-wing political groups have organized several committees to investigate the cause of the disturbances. Trade unions have also asked workers to maintain peace and return to work. (National Telegram, 10th)

(Paris) It has been learned here that the anti-government demonstrations and riots in various French seaports were planned by the Communist Party. This has been verified. Two Communist Party instructors immediately departed for the Communist Party branch in Brest after the outbreak of the riots to give final instructions. It is claimed that of the 85 people arrested in the Toulon riots, only 12 are over 20 years old. One of the 36 people currently detained has been confirmed to be a grammar school teacher. Britain Prepares for General Election to be Held in October 51

(London) The current British Parliament was elected in 1931 and is now scheduled to hold a general election in October. Various political parties are now engaged in large-scale activities to prepare for the election. The number of candidates who have been nominated is 1,473, including 490 belonging to the government party, 50 belonging to the Simon-led Liberal Party, and 28 belonging to the National Labour Party. The number of candidates belonging to the opposition party is 505 belonging to the Labour Party and 400 belonging to the Samuel-led Liberal Party. This number of candidates is not yet fixed, as the total number of candidates will increase, while the number of candidates from the Samuel-led Liberal Party may decrease. In addition, former Liberal Prime Minister Lloyd George may put forward candidates under the banner of a revival platform, but it is currently uncertain. As for the Conservative Party, it intends to find ways to increase the number of candidates from the Simon-led Liberal Party and the National Labour Party, and to have some Conservative candidates give up their candidacies so that the National Cabinet can win. Recently, Conservative Party leader Prime Minister Baldwin issued a declaration reaffirming the banner of the National Cabinet and asking voters to trust it. It can be seen that the Conservative Party does not intend to campaign alone, but wants to unite with the National Labour Party and the Simon-led Liberal Party to fight against the opposition party. (Havas, 9th)

There is Another Labor Strike in the United States, 15,000 People Reject Work Relief Plan 52

(New York) 15,000 skilled workers today refused to work for the government's work relief plan, which may halt the project and leave another 105,000 workers unemployed. Green, the president of the American Federation of Labor, said that similar strikes may occur in Chicago, Cleveland, San Francisco, and Seattle. It is generally believed that this move will make the situation take a sharp turn for the worse. Whether union workers can force the government to pay union workers the wages they deserve can be determined by this move. Federal Relief Commissioner Hopkins criticized the matter in Washington, saying that work relief workers will never go on strike. If they do not want to work, they can go elsewhere. At the same time, New York Work Relief Commissioner General Johnson warned striking workers not to brew riots, but the striking workers paid no attention to it. New York General Federation of Labor Chairman Mounet sent a flight group to encourage non-union workers to join the strike, further complicating the situation. (National Telegram, 9th)

(Washington) President Roosevelt declared today that work relief workers must accept the minimum wage, otherwise they will lose their jobs completely. The President denied the report that union skilled workers at the New York Work Relief Office had gone on strike, and said that he would not force workers to work. (National Telegram, 9th)

Atlantic City The President of the American Federation of Labor, Green, said today that the union will continue to oppose the minimum wage and said, "I warn that unfortunate things are about to happen. We have done everything we can. Our policies have been expressed, and we do not want to take further action." (National Telegram, 9th)

If they reject the government's plan, they will lose their right to receive relief. (Reuters, 9th)

(New York) The strike of workers at the New York City Engineering Works Bureau has now been realized, but the number is small, only 727. US Senate Passes Social Security Act, Now Submitted to President Roosevelt for Signature

(Washington) The Senate passed the Social Security Act today and sent it to the White House for President Roosevelt's signature. (National Telegram, 9th)

(Washington) The Social Security Act, which the government submitted to Congress earlier, was passed by both the Senate and the House of Representatives in June, and then amended by a joint conference of the two houses. The Senate today passed the amended version of the bill. The bill provides for unemployment insurance and worker pension systems, and is the most important bill in the Congressional agenda. Its purpose is to enable the American people to rely on pensions paid by the federal and state governments, as well as national unemployment insurance and pension systems, without having to suffer the pain of unemployment, poverty, or old age. It is expected that President Roosevelt will sign it into law. The cost of this bill is approximately US$3 billion, of which only one-tenth is raised through taxation, and the rest is contributed by employers and employees each year. The fund for this contribution increases year by year, and it is estimated that the total amount will reach US$50 billion in 1980. At that time, men and women over the age of 65 will receive a government subsidy of up to US$85 per month in pensions. (Havas, 9th)

—Reuters Special Business Telegram, August 10—

Gold and Silver

English Gold: The London gold price today was 140 shillings and 5 pence, down half a pence.

English Silver: The London silver market was quiet today, with prices unchanged. Spot is still at 30 pence .1875, futures at 30 pence .25. The United States bought in, India both bought and sold, China sold out, and the market closed steadily.

Exchange Rates

Anglo-American: The London foreign exchange market was stable this morning, with the price of the pound slightly stronger against the dollar and little change against the franc. The opening price of the Anglo-American exchange rate was $4.966875, up .1875 from yesterday's closing price. It rose .125 in the first hour, fell at noon, and rose again before closing. The closing price was $4.968125.

Anglo-French: The opening price rose 3 points, to 74 francs .96. The fluctuations throughout the day were very narrow. The closing price was 74 francs .94.

Cotton and Wheat

American Cotton: The New York cotton market continued to be sluggish. Speculative interest was still lacking. Although officials from the State Council opposed cotton loans, the market opened slightly higher due to good Liverpool telegrams and continued reports of very high temperatures in the central and western cotton belts.

American Wheat: Chicago wheat prices were slightly higher today due to yesterday's government estimates favoring the bulls and favorable telegrams from Liverpool. Coarse grains opened slightly higher, especially in the near term, but later returned to around yesterday's closing prices.

English Cotton: The Liverpool cotton market rose slightly today, in sympathy with yesterday's American market. The closing price for October was 6.03, up 5 points.

English Wheat: The Liverpool wheat market continued to rise today due to bullish telegrams from the United States. The closing price for October was 5 shillings 3 and 1/8 pence, up 1 and 1/8 pence.

Securities

Inspection Report on Flood Disaster Along Rivers 82

— Special Correspondent Geng Ya

Unprecedented Tianmen Flood Disaster

A small boat rowed out from Huangjia Bridge in the early morning, winding its way through the drainage ditches of Longshu. Every time it passed a house, the boatman would call out to ask if anyone was going to the city. Those who responded boarded, totaling twelve people. It was said that because everyone nearby lived on higher ground, boats were scarce, so they had to call out to make arrangements. After about two miles, they arrived at Wujia Changwan. They abandoned the boat and waded through the mud. The villagers who had not been drowned or displaced were engaged in repairing houses and removing mud, but their movements were slow and they lacked energy. It was clear that without repairs, the situation would be untenable, yet the repairs seemed utterly pointless. According to them, there were more than sixty households in the village. When the flood came, everyone climbed onto the roofs and went hungry for three days and nights before the water receded enough for them to come down. Chickens, dogs, pigs, and cattle had all drowned, their bloated corpses emitting a foul stench. The situation was extremely tragic. At that time, the sound of weeping filled the city, and there were occasional gunshots. It was initially thought that the security team was shooting at water monsters, but it later turned out they were intimidating and forcing the people to hand over their boats for their own use.

Leaving the village, they waded through accumulated water, which was knee-deep. There were branches that tripped them up. Near the edge, they saw soybeans, but only the stalks remained, without any leaves. A woman stood far away, shouting angrily, saying, "After the flood, you shouldn't trample on my soybean field again. I'm afraid it will be impossible to find even a bit of firewood." Approaching the woman, they saw she was holding a naked infant with a swollen belly and skeletal frame, which was very pitiful. Crossing the Tianmen County River, they arrived at the street along the city moat. Looking up at the mud deposited on the rooftops, they knew that the water level had receded about fifteen feet. However, the Xiang River embankment had collapsed without being blocked, and the flow of the county river was still very strong. The water levels of the 民十 and 民二十 were very high, but neither reached the street along the embankment. This year, however, the water rose three feet above the street along the embankment, five feet higher than the highest water level of 民十. The severity of the disaster can be imagined. The street along the embankment was a gathering place for hundreds of merchants, and the essence of Tianmen. Shops stood side by side, and the offices of government officials were not completely free of water. They were temporarily using a drugstore on the street along the embankment as an office. They then visited Commissioner and County Magistrate Shi Youping, who informed them of the general situation of the Tianmen flood as follows:

Tianmen has low-lying terrain, and the Xiang River and County River run through it. The people depend on the embankments for their lives. On July 7th, the Xiang River embankment in the Zhongxiang County area breached in three or four sections. From its high position, the area along the County River was the first to be impacted and was completely submerged. Unfortunately, the Shuanghe area in the fourth district of the county also suffered a breach, and seventy-two villages were turned into a watery expanse. The water rose exceptionally rapidly, rising more than nineteen feet in a day and night. The extent of the disaster was unprecedented. After the breach in Zhongxiang on the 7th, Tianmen heard the news on the 8th and telegraphed the county magistrates of Zhongxiang and Jingshan, but received no response because the telegraph poles had been destroyed, resulting in a disruption of communication. Shi immediately led engineer Liu Shengheng and others to Yuekou to supervise the protection. Fortunately, the stationed troops joined the rescue efforts, and no accidents occurred. However, the floodwaters reached Tianmen at about 1 p.m., steadily rising until 8 a.m. on the 9th, when they suddenly overflowed the embankment and breached it. More than a dozen members of the rescue security team and laborers were washed away. The western section of the moat embankment overflowed and breached in thirteen places, both large and small. About three hundred families in the Ximen area were severely affected. Except for the north and south city gate towers and the top of the ancient city embankment outside the north gate, there was no dry land left in the entire city. By evening, the entire city was submerged, filled with cries for help. In addition, the wind and waves roared, and the mountains seemed to shake. The human world and the realm of ghosts were almost indistinguishable.

It was found that the breached area was more than twenty feet higher than Tianmen County (calculated according to the Wusong Datum), so when the water reached Tianmen, it rushed and poured down, causing the most severe damage. Furthermore, the area below Tianmen, including Hanchuan and Hanyang, is even lower than Tianmen. Therefore, although the water level has now receded, Hanchuan and Hanyang are still submerged. In total, in Tianmen County, except for the third, sixth, and seventh districts, which are on higher ground and were not flooded, all other areas are a vast expanse of water. The disaster area is approximately 6,300 li, accounting for seven-eighths of the entire county. The affected population is approximately 124,000 households, or 643,000 people, accounting for eight-tenths of the entire county's population. Approximately 1.4 million mu of farmland were flooded, accounting for eight-tenths of the county's farmland. The loss of housing, crops, clothing, livestock, etc., is no less than 25 million yuan. The number of people drowned is approximately 12,000. Public losses, such as telephone lines, county roads, district roads, and public buildings such as government offices, Confucian temples, various agencies, schools, newly built碉樓, newly built city walls, etc., are estimated to be no less than 300,000 yuan. This spring, in order to improve the rural economy and production, 83,000 mulberry seedlings were requested from the Economic Commission, and they had grown more than a foot tall. Three thousand two hundred dan of selected cotton seeds were requested from the Provincial Construction Department, and they had been planted and were blooming. Now, all of this has been lost.

Relief measures include: (1) providing work as relief, urgently repairing the breached areas to prevent the cities of Tianmen and Hanyang from continuing to be threatened by floods; (2) providing loans for seeds and draught cattle to allow people to take advantage of the receding waters to plant crops; (3) the more than ten breaches in the moat embankment should be repaired immediately, estimated to require 59,000 yuan in labor relief costs (excluding items 1 and 2). All expenses depend on donations from all parties. Currently, the province has provided 13,000 yuan in relief funds and慰勞金, 1,300 bags of flour, and 1,225 packages of broad beans, which is a drop in the bucket and difficult to meet the needs. It is hoped that there will be a continuous flow of aid so that life can gradually return to normal.

After the reporter took his leave, he entered the city to inspect the situation. Shi sent his adjutant, Kuang Jichu, as a guide. The county seat is located on low-lying land, so a moat embankment about thirty-two li long was built to prevent floods. The county river flows around its southwest, east and north sides for about twenty-four li. Therefore, the lives and property of the entire city depended on the protection of the moat embankment. This time, the moat embankment itself went bankrupt, with more than thirty breaches of varying sizes, causing the entire city to be turned into a watery expanse and creating an unprecedented disaster. Walking west along the street along the embankment to Yishuiguan Zhoujia Lane, the floodwaters overflowed the embankment and poured into the lane, scouring it into a pit several dozen feet deep. Houses collapsed, and people were killed and injured, as if a huge bomb had been dropped by an airplane. Xidi Xia Street and Zhong Street also had breaches, with similar situations, but the devastation was even more severe.

Taking a boat into the city, they first passed the Xita Temple. The temple was built in the Jin Dynasty and had a long history, but now it has been completely destroyed, with only three old trees remaining. Arriving at the city wall, the water was still blocking the east, north, and west gate arches. The boat entered through a breach in the west city wall. They saw the Central Primary School (with twelve classes, well-run) and the Land Survey Office, with water levels reaching the doors and windows. The old and dilapidated houses of the common people were even more severely damaged. Entering the Commissioner's Office, a woman was paddling a door in the front yard. The offices, reception rooms, and flower gardens were on higher ground, and the receding water had left a foot of mud, making cleaning difficult. Leaving through the back door, they climbed the north city gate tower. Thirty-four male and female prisoners were being held there. Eighty prisoners were also being held in the south city gate tower. They had all been moved from the prison during the flood. The towers were small and crowded, and sitting and standing were already difficult. Sleeping at night must be even more cramped. Being confined in such a way in the hot weather was very pitiful. The guards were from the Sixteenth Company, and the captain, Zhao Pi, was known for maintaining military discipline, so his reputation was still good. The north and south main streets inside the city were visible, but the outside north was still a vast flood.

Taking the original boat from under the north city gate, they circled the west gate. Waves lapped against the gate arch, making a soft sound. There were many grass sheds on the city wall. Refugees were washing clothes and drawing water by the city, as if living by the embankment. More than a hundred civilian houses were destroyed in the Ximen area, with no tiles or bricks visible. However, when the water receded on the thirteenth and fourteenth, many corpses were hanging from the trees. Walking into the city from the south gate, some shops on South Main Street had opened, but the western part was still gloomy like hell. Because many people were crushed by collapsed houses, there was a foul stench, and they dared not go near to inquire.

The Terrible Situation of Tianmen Being Flooded

Returning to say goodbye to Commissioner Shi, he insisted on keeping them for a meal. During the meal, they learned that Shi had drafted a management plan for the Xiang River flood, which stated, "The Xiang River contains a large amount of sediment, which easily silts up the riverbed, making it futile to increase the height of the embankment. Prevention is impossible, and dredging the Xiang River, which has a sandy bottom, is also difficult. Large-scale reservoirs should be built in the mountainous areas of Shaanxi Province, and the water levels should be reported to the middle and lower reaches at any time. In the middle reaches, measures should be taken to maintain the riverbanks, and in the lower reaches, more tributaries should be opened to divert the water flow. In this way, flood prevention can be effective." Building reservoirs in the upper reaches and reporting water levels are fundamental plans, and the authorities in charge of water conservancy must already be considering them.

In addition, there are three other things related to the Tianmen disaster that should be mentioned. First, when the floodwaters came ashore and destroyed the homes of more than thirty residents on Lower Embankment Street, Yang Dazhen, the father of 保長 Yang Lunji, seeing the dangerous situation, urgently hired two boats at a high price to load his family and neighbors Zheng Yongsheng, Shen Yixing, Zhang Yunqing, and the two families of Chen Yongxing, totaling thirty men and women, and carried their clothes, chests, money, and other items. They stopped behind Shen Yixing's back door. Unexpectedly, five soldiers from the Fifteenth Company of the Security Team (including one pockmarked messenger carrying a box cannon) came and demanded one of the boats. If they refused, they would open fire. Yang Dazhen and others obeyed and crowded into one boat, which was rocking and about to sink. They called for help from another boat. The clothes and chests of money that had been handed over to the previous boat were not taken out. The soldiers forced the boat to leave quickly, and the boat crowded with Yang Dazhen and others capsized into the water, drowning more than twenty people. In addition, several cases of extorting money during the rescue occurred. Fortunately, Commissioner Shi returned from Yuekou early, and the security situation was turned from danger to safety. Regarding the tragic case of奪船 drowning people, it was reported that the family members of the deceased, Yang Lunji, knelt and "攔馬喊寃" when the commissioner inspected the embankment. The commissioner was moved and punished the offenders.

Second, in Xinhe, a township in the western part of Tianmen, there was a female hero, Wang Li, who, when the floodwaters suddenly arrived and people climbed onto the roofs, crying and in a desperate situation, Wang Li was able to bravely disregard her own safety and row back and forth, rescuing more than two hundred disaster victims without accepting a penny. Recently, Li Shucheng, the head of the provincial inspection team, heard about this and deeply admired her, and especially represented the provincial government to award Wang Li forty yuan. In addition, there was also a boatman, Yang Gou, who automatically rescued hundreds of people and was also awarded twenty yuan.

Third, there is an organization called "Tea Party" that uses the name of providing tea and doing charitable work to solicit donations and public virtue, and uses various retributional superstitions such as "heaven collapsing and earth cracking" and "red rain flood" to scare people into joining the association. Those who are superstitious, in addition to donating money and gifts, are even forced by the gods to sell their property to fill the association's funds. It is said that in this way, when a great disaster occurs, they can ride a new broom to heaven, or fly with new shoes, or hold knives and spears, close their eyes, and kill randomly to the north, and the Bodhisattva will come to save them. The association was founded in 1927 or 1928, and no one paid attention to it at first. Its followers spread throughout Tianmen, Jingshan, and Mianyang counties. The original intention was to borrow the gods to collect money, but recently their actions have shown a trend towards becoming the Yellow Turban Rebels, the White Lotus Sect, or the Boxers. The Security Headquarters arrested several leaders, and the remaining followers were still planning to come to the city to rob the prison when the flood inundated the city. Fortunately, the defenses were strong, and the future can be assured of safety.

Song Sa

Tracing Stolen Goods

The robbery case of Jiang Sigen and others in Caoking Xihuo Tangxiang has been investigated by the Ninth Sub-Precinct of that area. It has been discovered that villagers Yao Aba and Sun Yuanqing are suspected of being involved and have left the area together. It was later learned that Sun Yuanqing was hiding in the home of his father-in-law, Lu Zimin. The sub-precinct went to Lu's residence to search without making any noise. Sun Yuanqing had already escaped after hearing the news. Two chests were found upstairs, containing more than ten silk garments, which were not items used by farming families. Lu Zimin confessed that they were brought by his son-in-law, Sun Yuanqing. The sub-precinct then sent Lu Zimin and the stolen goods to the County Public Security Bureau for review and handling.

Public Official Fined for Visiting Prostitute

Zhang Youlan, a staff member of the Land Bureau from Jiangyin, is in his sixties and has a penchant for womanizing. Yesterday evening at about 11 p.m., he and two laborers went to the Jiaotong Inn on Changqiao Street after drinking in the western outskirts and hired a prostitute named Chen Xiubao in room number four. They were caught by inspectors from the Second Sub-Precinct, who considered it detrimental to public morals and took them to the bureau for questioning and fined them five yuan. It is said that someone with influence later bailed him out.

Kunshan

Lake Bandits Attempt to Rob Zhouxiang Town

At 8:30 p.m. on the 9th, several dozen lake bandits were discovered in the Sanchongwan area near the Wusong River in the Sixth District. They were armed with guns and were on eight bandit boats of various sizes, planning to rob Zhouxiang Town. The local villagers noticed and urgently reported to Wang Dasan, the chief of the Third Branch of the Zhangpu Town Public Security Bureau, and Xu Mengzeng, the leader of the First Squad of the Ninth Provincial Security Team stationed in Daci Town. They immediately led the police force to suppress and capture the bandits. By the time they arrived, the bandits had not yet landed. The police force immediately opened fire. Seeing that they were prepared, the bandits resisted slightly and jumped onto their boats, retreating into the Wusong River. The police force bravely pursued them, sinking six bandit boats and capturing six lake bandits, who were taken to the Third Branch for detention.

Private Trafficking of Opium Sentenced to Ten Years

Zhang Da, the head of the Anti-Smoking Investigation Section of the County Public Security Bureau, has spared no effort in investigating and suppressing private opium. Yesterday afternoon at 1 p.m., Zhang learned that Zhang Zaili in the Baziqiao area outside the North Gate was specializing in selling opium. He immediately ordered Fang Zheng, the head of the investigation team, to lead detectives to arrest Zhang. Thirty liang of Guo Yuanmao brand opium were found and taken to the County Anti-Smoking Committee. After questioning by the committee, it was confirmed that Zhang Zaili was indeed selling opium and was sentenced to ten years in prison as a warning.

Changshu

Rising River Water Endangers Dike

Recently, there have been storms and rain here, coupled with the overflowing of the river tide. The autumn flood is particularly large, resulting in a 550-meter-long section of the dike along the Xu Liu Jing River in this county being found to be extremely dangerous by the patrol officer, requiring urgent repairs. The estimated cost is 18,000 yuan. The county government has reported this and initially allocated 2,000 yuan from the water conservancy fund to cover the cost. The remaining amount has been submitted to the province for review. An order has been received to first repair the most dangerous 130-odd zhang. The county has purchased 麻袋, wooden stakes, and stones and transported them to Xu Liu Jing for repairs.

Wuxi

Robbery Occurs at Lumberyard in Bustling City

At 0:30 p.m. yesterday (the 10th), two villagers and a carpenter arrived at the Shen Fengyu lumberyard in Pengxia Street outside Ximen to purchase two sets of coffin lumber. Wan Youkun, the manager of the lumberyard, and his partners Rong Kuifu greeted them. The price was agreed upon as 70 yuan. The villagers took out 55 yuan in paper money and 15 yuan in silver and handed it over to manager Wan Youkun to put in the drawer of the accounting table. However, a thief saw this and was tempted. He sneaked into the counter, grabbed the 70 yuan, and ran straight out. Fortunately, partner Rong Kuifu saw this and shouted, "Robbery!" He immediately led the crowd to chase after the thief. Seeing that the situation was not good, the thief threw all the money down and fled. Rong and the others saw that the thief had escaped and the money had been recovered, so they returned to the shop. The manager reported the information to the Public Security Bureau and requested an investigation.

Drug Ring Fugitive Xiao Junfa Arrested

The Supervision Department of the Public Security Bureau of this county received a secret report a few days ago that Xiao Junfa (also known as Xiao Wuxi), a shareholder of drug king Wang Guiqing, had fled to Tianjin and Shanghai after Wang Guiqing's case was exposed. Now, hearing that the situation had calmed down, he had secretly returned to Wuxi and was hiding in the home of his concubine Chen Yueying at No. 14 Wang Lane, Guqiao. They requested an investigation. Chief Inspector Wang received the report and immediately dispatched inspector Ge Xinde to lead police officers to search. They arrested Xiao and found one and a half快上快 pills, 26 empty paper bags, 332 yuan in paper money, and an empty 太古 sugar tin box. They took him to the bureau for strict questioning. Xiao Junfa confessed that in February 1933, he and Wang Guiqing, Zheng Deliang, Su Guoliang (also known as Su Lanbao), and others each contributed more than 3,000 yuan to manufacture small gray Guo Fusheng毒嬌. After Wang Guiqing and the others' cases were exposed, he fled to Tianjin. Today, he returned to Wuxi to visit his concubine and was unfortunately arrested. He was transferred to the county government yesterday (the 10th) for investigation and handling.

Nantong

Preventing Flooding from the Yangtze River

The Nantong riverbank has been collapsing rapidly recently, with many breaches along the riverbank, creating a dangerous situation. With the autumn floods approaching, the tide is overflowing, causing significant impact. Representatives from all sectors have urgently decided that in addition to the Construction Bureau preparing for prevention, they will immediately send a telegram to the provincial government, forwarding it to the central government and the flood prevention committee, and the Yangtze River Commission to send personnel to investigate. Chen Baochu has been appointed as a representative to petition the province and the central government separately.

Yangzhou

Dike on North Bank of Yangtze River in Critical Condition

The easterly wind has been blowing strongly for days, and the river tide has suddenly risen, causing many dangerous sections along the north bank of the Yangtze River, such as the dikes in the Second District of this county from Longwang Temple east to Doutian Temple, to be repeatedly and violently scoured by the wind and waves. County Magistrate Ma Zhenbang and Director of the Construction Bureau Shu Guohua have been paying special attention to the riverside dike project due to the unusually strong wind. They have sent technician Zhang Hanqing to purchase materials and summon farmers from the villages where the dikes are located to carry out night-time repairs. However, one section of the old bank of Gongliuwei, 478 meters long from east to west, was finally completed after several attempts at prevention. Unexpectedly, on the morning of the 8th, about 221 meters of the eastern section of the 圩 suddenly collapsed, and dozens of mu of farmland and several houses were washed away. Fortunately, it was during the day, and no one was injured. Currently, the remaining western section and the small堤 along the north and south banks are 330 meters long. Dozens of leaks have been found at the bottom of the western bank, which is 249 meters long, and the situation is critical. The farmers are being urged to do everything they can to repair the dikes. However, the wind and waves are becoming increasingly dangerous, and it is difficult to predict whether the situation can be resolved without problems. However, there is a large堤 in the 圩, about five or six meters wide, which is the dike body newly built in 1932. It is uncertain whether it can withstand the river tide. According to technician Zhang, in addition to doing everything possible to repair the missing sections, the currently un-collapsed but dangerous western section is being defended and guarded by gathering laborers to work overnight. Precautions are also being taken for the inner large堤, and they can only do their best and wait for the weather to improve. Today (the 10th), technician Zhang has submitted a report on the repairs to the Construction Bureau, which will be forwarded to the county government.

Flood Disaster: First Joint Meeting of Directors and Supervisors Held Yesterday 83

Resolved: To Apply for Issuance of Flood Relief Bonds, To Borrow 500,000 Yuan from Various Banks

Xu Shiying Went to Nanjing Last Night and Will Stay Briefly Before Going North to Inspect the Disaster

The first joint meeting of directors and supervisors of the Shanghai Fundraising Association for Flood Relief in Various Provinces was held at 4 p.m. yesterday at the Renji Hall. The meeting was chaired by Xu Shiying, the vice president of the association. Several important resolutions were passed. The details are as follows:

Attendees

The attendees included Chairman Kong Xiangxi (represented by Huang Yindan), Vice Chairmen Xu Shiying and Wu Tiecheng (represented by Li Dachao), and Wang Yansong, Pan Gongzhan, Wang Boqi, Lu Wenzhong, Yan Fuqing, Han Juemin, Du Yuesheng, Wen Lanting, Zhao Jinqing, Chen Jicheng, Li Wuyun, Zhao Yiwu, Quan Shaowu, Lin Kanghou, Li Zicai, Wang Xiaolai, Li Dachao, Feng Yangshan, Li Jingchen, Zhu Shaoping, Wang Peiyuan, Pan Liangyu, Qu Wenliu, Huang Renzhi, Ding Guicen, Shi Weijun, Gu Guanyuan, Sun Choucheng, Lu Bohong, Huang Bodu, and more than fifty others.

Resolutions Passed

After the customary formalities, Vice Chairman Xu reported on (1) the format of the donation receipt and (2) the draft of the public notice to be published in the newspapers. Then, the discussion began, and the following resolutions were passed: 1. In view of the urgent need for relief in Hubei, Shandong, and other provinces, the association will first borrow 300,000 yuan from the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications, and borrow another 200,000 yuan from other banks to carry out urgent relief efforts. Mayor Wu, Wang Yiting, Du Yuesheng, Xu Shiying, Wang Xiaolai, Yu Zuoting, Zhang Xiaolin, Zhao Jinqing, Chen Guangfu, Lin Kanghou, Lu Bohong, and other gentlemen were elected to be responsible for representing the association. Mayor Wu will be responsible for convening a meeting next Monday (the 12th) to discuss the arrangements. 2. To petition the Central Government and the National Government to issue flood relief bonds for the 24th year of the Republic of China. 3. The planning and fundraising groups will meet at the association at 4 p.m. on Tuesday (the 13th) to discuss ways to raise relief funds and supplies. 4. Due to the widespread epidemic in the disaster area, there is an urgent need for medicine. The association will send personnel to the Chinese and Western medicine trade associations and major Chinese and Western drug stores to collect medicines for distribution in the disaster area. The director of the health group will plan to establish medical and pharmaceutical rescue teams to go to the disaster areas for rescue. 5. The association's administrative expenses will be kept to a minimum. As in the previous drought relief effort, the chairman will allocate separate funds and will not spend a single cent from the fundraising. 6. Whether to distribute cash or food for this emergency relief effort will be decided by the investigation and distribution group, taking into account the actual situation, formulating a plan, and submitting it to the standing committee for approval, with the principle of meeting the urgent needs of the disaster victims. 7. All groups of the association should immediately strengthen their organization and hold a joint meeting at the association at 4 p.m. next Wednesday (the 13th) to discuss all ongoing matters.

Motions

After the discussion of the motions, the following temporary motions were passed: (1) Ye Chucang was additionally appointed as vice chairman of the association, Pan Gongzhan was appointed as director of the design group, and Wu Xingya and Jin Tingxun were appointed as standing directors of the association. (2) Vice Chairman Xu proposed that this emergency relief effort should not directly send personnel to distribute aid, but should entrust the provincial governments' relief committees or the general flood relief association to investigate and distribute the aid. The association will send personnel to investigate and monitor the situation. This motion should be submitted to the investigation and distribution group for review and a plan to be submitted to the association for deliberation.

Xu Went to Nanjing Yesterday

Xu Shiying has successfully established the flood relief association in Shanghai that he planned to organize during this trip. All the association's affairs are also proceeding actively. In addition to leaving his secretary, Huang Bodu, in Shanghai to handle all the association's affairs on a regular basis, Xu went to Nanjing on the special express train to Nanjing at 11 p.m. last night with his son, Xu Gongshi, as Shandong and other provinces urged him to go and inspect the disaster. After a brief stay in Nanjing, he will go north to inspect the disaster situation.
