Ice Cream and Thermoses (Common Sense) 162

— Junpeng

Hey! Little friends who have eaten ice cream! Do you know how ice cream is made? Perhaps not! Let me tell you, roughly, ice and salt are mixed in a ratio of two to one and placed outside a mixture of milk, eggs, and other ingredients. At this point, as the ice melts into water and the salt dissolves into the water, both absorb a considerable amount of heat. As a result, the surrounding temperature drops to minus twenty-two degrees Celsius, thus freezing the milk and other ingredients into a solid – ice cream. It is because ice melts into water, absorbing a large amount of heat, that the melting of ice can create a quite low temperature. The cause is based on this principle.

The day before yesterday, I went to Shanghai for fun and bought some ice cream, which I put in a thermos to bring back. When I got home and poured it out, the ice cream hadn't melted at all. Little friends, do you know why? Let me first explain how a thermos keeps the water inside warm. A thermos is a double-walled glass bottle with the air evacuated from between the walls, and the inner and outer surfaces of the double walls are silver-plated. The reason is that glass is a poor conductor, sufficient to prevent conduction; evacuating the air between the walls is sufficient to prevent conduction and convection; and silver-plating the inner and outer surfaces is sufficient to prevent heat from escaping and cold air from entering. Therefore, putting cold ice cream inside can prevent external heat from entering and internal cold air from escaping. If you don't believe it, you can try it. Little friends who live in the countryside can follow my method, take it home for your families to taste the flavor of ice cream, and at the same time, gain a lot of common sense.

Plowing 163

Airplane 164

— Chong

Little friends! Now I am going to introduce you to making a toy, which is the airplane necessary for national defense. Making this kind of airplane is very fun. It can fly in the sky and move on the ground. If you don't believe it, you might as well try making it according to the instructions below, or make it with your classmates. Make one each, and hold a "flying competition" to see whose flies faster. Isn't that very interesting?

Tools and materials: Several sections of bamboo poles, iron wire (lead wire can also be used as a substitute), a small square lead sheet, about half a square inch, two rubber bands (rubber bands), three feet of thread, wheels from old toys, silk (sold in large stationery stores). Scissors, a small knife, an eraser, a pen, ink, an inkstone, etc. Once these are prepared, then start making it. When making it, first, be careful; second, make sure that it is not heavier on one side than the other. With these two conditions, you won't have to worry about it not succeeding.

Method: According to Figure A, use bamboo to carve the leaves that rotate on the nose of the plane. Figure B is also carved from bamboo to make two wings. Figure C; you need to make two of these, for the fuselage. Figure D; is for the crossbar at the tail of the fuselage, with two eye bolts installed on it (sold in hardware stores, buy the smallest ones). Figure E; is a border made of thin iron wire, with thin silk pasted on it, and the two wings behind the fuselage are made in the same way as Figure E. Figure F; is what it looks like after it is assembled. Figure G; is what the nose looks like. Figure H; is what the tail looks like. At its very end, use wire to connect it to the rear crossbar to serve as a rear wheel.

Dimensions, as indicated in the diagram, or you can enlarge or reduce them as you like. However, if you enlarge it, you must enlarge everything proportionally; you cannot enlarge the fuselage and not enlarge the wings. That won't be successful. If you want to reduce it, do the opposite.

How to play: First, wind the rubber band tightly, and don't let it loosen. Then place it on a smooth floor, and when you release your hand, it will walk on the ground. If you want to make it fly, you can also do that. First, complete the steps above, then take it to the balcony on the second floor and toss it into the air, and it will fly forward.

Children's Novel

The Little Drummer Boy (II) 166

— Xin Qing

The little drummer boy ran upstairs after him and entered a dilapidated top floor room. He saw the Major holding paper and a pencil, leaning against the window sill, with a long rope on the floor beside him.

The Major folded the paper, fixed his cold, gray-brown eyes on the little drummer boy's face, and suddenly said, "Drummer!"

The little drummer boy raised his hand to the brim of his hat and saluted.

The Major said: "Are you brave?"

The little drummer boy's eyes brightened, and he replied: "Yes, Major!"

The Major walked with him to the window and said: "Look down there, near the Faranga Villa, there are many bayonets glittering on the ground. That's our military camp. Take this paper, climb down the window with this rope, dash across the small mountain like lightning, run across the field, and deliver this paper to the first officer you meet in our military camp. Now, take off your belt and backpack."

The little drummer boy took off his belt and backpack and hid the paper in the pocket in his chest; the sergeant threw the rope out of the window sill and held the end of the rope tightly; the Major helped the little drummer boy climb out of the window, his back facing the field.

The Major said: "Be careful, the salvation of the first detachment here depends entirely on your courage and your two legs."

"Major, please trust me," the little drummer boy replied. And he slid down the rope.

The Major held the rope tightly and said: "When you land, you have to crouch low on the ground."

"Don't worry, there's nothing to be afraid of."

"May God help you!"

Before long, the little drummer boy had reached the ground. The sergeant retracted the rope and immediately walked away, while the Major stood by the small window, watching the little drummer boy run down the small mountain. He hoped that he would not be seen by the enemy, but soon five or six small puffs of smoke rose from the ground. He knew that the boy had been discovered by the Austrian soldiers, who were firing down from the top of the mountain. The puffs of smoke were the sand and soil kicked up by the bullets hitting the ground. But the little drummer boy ignored everything and ran forward desperately. After a while, the Major cried out: "Oh no, he's dead!" But before his cry was over, he saw the little drummer boy had gotten up.

The Major couldn't help but breathe a sigh of relief and said, "Ah, he just fell!"

The little drummer boy was still running forward, but he was limping uncomfortably.

"He sprained his foot," the Major muttered.

Women's Forum

Disaster Relief and Disaster Prevention 167

— Jenny

This newspaper's Nanjing special dispatch on the 5th: "The Capital Women's Disaster Relief Association telegraphed to Chengdu and Qingdao, to the wives of Chiang and Wang, stating that the water disasters in the provinces of Hunan, Hubei, Jiangxi, Shandong, Anhui, Henan, Fujian were severe. The Association initiated a disaster relief association on the 5th and respectfully requests them to serve as initiators, and to solicit relief funds immediately to help the disaster victims. They also requested to be informed of everything by telegram. The Association also issued a declaration, asking women from all over the country to advocate together... and, if necessary, send personnel to the disaster areas to investigate the disaster situation in various places."

At this moment, when the cry of "Women Go Home" is sung to the clouds, it is indeed a joyous thing that the women of the capital can still take care of matters outside the home and initiate a disaster relief association. However, we believe that rather than saying "send personnel to the disaster areas to investigate if necessary," it would be better to definitively request the wives of important party and state figures to personally lead the wives and grandmothers leisurely enjoying life in their comfortable mansions to visit the disaster areas. They should know that the wives and grandmothers of the upper class are pampered and do not know the suffering of the world. This can make them aware that the hell on earth is just a short distance away. Perhaps this will allow them to save a little money from leisure and decoration expenses and save a few disaster victims gasping for breath in the flood!

Secondly, disaster relief is indeed the urgent task at present, but it is ultimately passive. The active thing is that everyone can recognize the root cause of this disaster. Especially the women's community, most of whom are superstitious, think that this is the victims' bad luck, and hold prayer meetings and disaster relief ceremonies. These not only cannot eliminate disasters, but are just a waste of life and money.

We know that droughts and floods are indeed natural disasters, but they can be eliminated by human effort. The reason why we do not have this kind of power to fight against natural disasters now is due to the weakness of our country and the unsoundness of the political and social system. Therefore, if we want to eliminate natural disasters forever, we must first strengthen the subjective strength of our society.

"Dispute Over Separate Schools for Boys and Girls in Beiping" 168

— Wu

Since the country has been gradually declining over the past few years, the issue of public morality has become louder and louder. Everyone knows that "public morality" cannot directly make people feel that it is a work of saving the country, like "aviation"; however, various places cannot help but make a fuss about it. When it gets exciting, it even spreads from "lowly" prostitutes and wandering singers to so-called "innocent" female students; many people are hoarse and exhausted from making a fuss about this, and their energy has found a place to be used.

Beiping is the most gloomy place, and there are many "generous people with sorrowful songs from Yan and Zhao" and people who have lost their homes in the Northeast. It is not easy to restrain their anger that wants to reach the stars! But now, the old well is stirring, and Mayor Yuan's insistence on separate schools for boys and girls in middle school has caused storms in the city, making people forget the situation of living in a precarious nest. It is true that the female students in the business, normal, and vocational departments who are merged into the general department will suffer losses, but after all, it is a small matter for "women". As long as it is convenient for the big things, the small things cannot be taken care of too much.

Moreover, doing things must adapt to the environment. The whole of China is like this, let alone Beiping? What is the use of those female students in Beiping who have specialized knowledge and skills, or higher scientific knowledge and higher world knowledge? Sooner or later, they will have to return to the corner of the house to learn "filial piety"! The horizontal line that men's education has already stepped on cannot be changed for a while, but women are easy to deal with. If you tell her to move out, she has to. After moving out, it doesn't matter whether you study in a women's school that promotes the doctrine of virtuous wives and good mothers or not. There are not many female students in the three northeastern provinces, and there are no middle schools with both male and female students; so there are very few girls who join their rebellions everywhere.

If the country wants to stretch its neck and see the light of day, then men and women can receive the same education in all kinds of knowledge and skills, and society can have more talents in various fields, which may be a help. But as I said just now: Beiping is the most cloudy place, and it is best for everyone to shrink their necks a little lower to show that it is a prosperous age. This matter should not be truly and frankly promoted, but should be done step by step: it is easier and more appropriate to start with the weaker female world. With a cry, the female students were told to return to the dim, restricted, and simple newly established girls' schools, and they had no choice but to obey. Using the reason that preventing adultery is better than preventing ..., many people also felt that "this is right!" Promotion is ultimately the work of great men with a few more tricks.

However, the representatives of private middle schools in Beiping are still holding meetings to strive to maintain "Beiping's inherent educational achievements." This seems to be just a matter of school prosperity, so what they are fighting for is just the school authorities. But, in reality, it is a crisis of women's education and a great threat to the women's community. After many years of hard struggle, they finally managed to knock on the door of men's schools and let women squeeze in, allowing them to hear more serious things besides being confined to being virtuous wives and good mothers, tailors and cooks; but now, under the false pretense of preventing suspicion, they are determined to make women retreat. If the matter in Beiping can still be regarded as a "national matter," it should be the women of the whole country and the men who want to see the light of day who should rise up and fight for it.

Now, it is only the middle school authorities of male and female students in Beiping who are rising up to fight for it, which is obviously turning a big matter into a small matter; and a small matter can be turned into nothing in the future. The separate schools for men and women in middle schools in Beiping will become a certainty. The situation of us shrinking our necks can be seen from Beiping and other places: Thus, dark clouds will lock the whole country, locking the women and men of the whole country.

Editorial Office

Women of Abyssinia 170

— Luo Qiong

Since the end of the 19th century, Abyssinia has been reduced to a semi-colony under the competition of Britain, France, and Italy. At present, it is the same as other semi-colonies, and has a tendency to gradually move from a semi-colony to a colony. Italy is the promoter of this trend. Now the Italian-Ethiopian dispute has reached a tense situation, and Ethiopia is unwilling to submit, and Italy is determined to use force to the end; the outbreak of war seems to be only a matter of time.

Since the dispute arose last winter, Ethiopia initially hoped for the League of Nations' fair judgment and the sanctions of the Non-Aggression Pact. However, the United States has stated that it does not want to interfere, and Britain and France are again seeking their own interests and cannot jointly maintain the credibility of the League of Nations. Under the control of this international situation, the Ethiopian authorities have only two paths to take: first, to surrender to Italy and accept all of Italy's demands unconditionally. The second is to prepare for a heroic national liberation war at any cost. The recent speeches of the Ethiopian King and the foreign statements of Ethiopian diplomats all indicate the determination to "rather die on the battlefield than lose an inch of land," which shows that Abyssinia is taking the second path.

In this war frenzy, the attitude of Ethiopian women is particularly noteworthy. According to the Havas dispatch of July 28th, "The Ethiopian Women's Assistance Army Committee held a meeting in the Ethiopian capital this afternoon, with the participation of military leaders, and resolved to organize groups to care for sick and wounded soldiers during wartime." Reuter's dispatch on the 30th of the same month stated that Ethiopian women are preparing to replace men's duties when men go to war. Ethiopian women can resolutely participate in the national war at this time of deepening national crisis; this is a good example for women in semi-colonies to follow.

Secondly, if the Ethiopian authorities take the aforementioned first path, then under the humiliating "good neighbor" diplomacy, it is inevitable that a retrograde "women go home" movement will be generated, that is, using household labor to trap women and paralyze their fighting consciousness. Not only does it hinder the liberation of women, but it sometimes indirectly helps imperialism, allowing it to smoothly carry out its aggression policy. However, the Ethiopian government is now taking the second path, and Ethiopian women have also bravely embarked on this second path. This is something we should learn from and admire!

Women's Issues Lecture

Lecture 8: Women in the Age of Imperialism 171

— Jun Hui

Section 1: World War and Women

Since the Industrial Revolution began at the end of the 18th century, for about a century, the world's capitalism, although occasionally encountering inevitable panics, generally saw a smooth upward development. The completion of industrial organization, the development of production technology, and the control of commodity and labor markets all demonstrated the highly developed form of capitalism. This led to the so-called imperialist era, the "final stage of capitalism."

However, European advanced countries, since the 15th century, had successively seized colonies as commodity markets in various parts of the world, and by this era, they had to re-divide them. As a result, the inherent contradictions of capitalism became increasingly acute. The economic protagonist of the century, Britain, and the emerging Germany engaged in a heated battle for market share. The economic competition developed into an arms race, leading to the unprecedented World War.

What was the result of the war? Ten million dead, twenty million wounded, and a total military expenditure of 400 billion yuan! For five whole years, the people of Europe struggled in poisonous gas and a sea of blood! In past history, this was the most brutal page!

However, merely listing these alarming numbers is not enough to express the true tragedy of the war. The truly painful tragedy, rather than being played out on the battlefield, was played out in the rear. Because the soldiers who rushed to the front lines, under the beautiful name of "dying for the motherland is glorious," even if they died from bullets, it was only a moment of pain. As for the mothers, wives, sons, and daughters of those soldiers in the rear, from the life-and-death separation at the time of departure to the receipt of the death notice, how many heartbreaking tears were shed, and how many illusory dreams were made! Living in the unbearable grief of wanting to cry but having no tears, what did "the glory of the motherland" have to do with them! What they wanted was the return of their husband or son! However, this was only a desperate fantasy! A long-term tragedy!

Clearly, this unprecedented bloody tragedy was something that the big capitalists of various countries urged their governments to launch in order to obtain commodity markets and more profits, but they also raised the banner of "for the motherland, for justice," encouraging soldiers to rush to the front lines as cannon fodder! Encouraging women to stay in the rear to maintain order! Of course, "patriotism is the highest justice"! Whoever dares to oppose this "justice" is a traitor! However, countless poor soldiers became sacrifices under the banners of "justice" and "patriotism"! The cruelty of the World War lies in this!

War not only robbed women of their husbands and sons, but also destroyed their livelihood – the family! In ordinary times, the husband or son was their economic "supporter" and the "master" of the family. But at this time, they became orphans and widows with nowhere to turn! Many proletarian women, in order to prolong this miserable life, had to find a way to survive! They either participated in the military-controlled munitions industry, doing unlimited labor in manufacturing killing tools, in order to barely survive, or they became prostitutes accompanying the army, or even joined bandit dens or revolutionary ranks.

Originally, capitalist governments in various countries, in order to indirectly boost the morale of soldiers on the front lines, raised the issue of guaranteeing the lives of their family members. That is, they stipulated that the wives, widows, and orphans of soldiers should be given monetary subsidies or other preferential treatment such as free accommodation. But these were "empty promises." Although women participating in work in the rear could support their own lives, the lives of their children and elderly relatives could not be maintained. Therefore, the infant mortality rate increased sharply during the war. In this way, the war not only robbed them of their husbands, but also robbed them of their children.

In this situation, women had no choice but to become reactionary elements of society. In the spring of 1915, working women in Berlin rose up to welcome revolutionary leaders Karl Liebknecht, attacking the Scheidemann government, and at the same time carried out anti-government demonstrations. Women in the warring countries raised strong protests against soaring prices and the cruel war. In 1916, women in Paris repeatedly destroyed markets and looted coal warehouses. In June 1916, women in Austria rebelled for "three days" to oppose the war and rising prices. In Italy, when the declaration of war began mobilization, women, unwilling to send their husbands and sons to the death line, formed human barricades with their bodies on the railway tracks to prevent the train from proceeding. The rebellion in Russia from St. Petersburg to Moscow, even spreading to various places in April 1915, was initiated by the wives of soldiers. In particular, the uprising of working women in St. Petersburg on March 8, 1917, became the fuse of the Russian Revolution. When capitalist governments preached "patriotism" to them, their reply was "We want to seize bread for our children"!

In this way, women experienced miserable lives in the Great War and resolutely opposed the war! But twenty years later, the so-called Second World War is inevitable and upon us! Judging from the general situation, this time the battlefield is likely to be in the Pacific Ocean, and China will naturally bear the brunt! It is said that this war will be more cruel and more extensive than the previous one! How should we women cope with this terrible tragedy of great destruction? This is a major issue to be seriously considered.

Medium-length fiction

Returning Home 172

— Su Hong

(4)

The snow was falling heavily, and the ground was already more than an inch thick. Many footprints were deeply imprinted on the same road. Beggars, in groups of three or four or four or five, walked back and forth, and the sound of "sisha, sisha" often came from the snow. Xiu Zhen carried a dirty pair of pants to the riverbank to wash. The river surface was covered with long, wide windows and heavy wooden cabinets. She looked up at the opposite bank. The black lacquered gate was wide open, and the workers were still carrying them out piece by piece and throwing them into the river. She carefully looked at it, whose home was that? Over the years, she had forgotten a bit. In the past, although the gate was black, it was not as newly black as it was now. On the roof, the tiles had been arranged neatly, the walls had been painted snow-white, and several bungalows had been added next to the house. But other than this house, there were no better houses. Either they were older and more dilapidated, or they had collapsed into ruins. The thatched shed at the foot of the mountain was left with only a few beams, lying there crookedly.

Xiu Zhen had just finished washing her pants and stood up when the sons of the Taigong carried a basket of white rice to wash. They brushed past her, almost knocking her down. She knew that the rice was for making New Year cakes, and she recalled the taste of New Year cakes. She also heard the sound of pounding New Year cakes next door, which aroused her appetite even more. She couldn't help but turned a corner and glanced at the snow-white, soft glutinous rice cakes that had just been steamed and were being pounded in the mortar in the Taigong's house.

Xiu Zhen, covered in snowflakes, entered the house. Before she could step inside, she saw her sister-in-law breastfeeding her young nephew. Her eldest nephew walked up to his mother and cried for something to eat. Her sister-in-law glanced at Xiu Zhen and loudly scolded her son:

"Little devil! You're coming over again! What do I have to give you to eat? I only have myself! You want to eat, 'you, big and small, might as well eat me up!'" The eldest nephew cried and shouted, and his sister-in-law scolded even more fiercely, giving him a severe beating and then throwing the child out into the snow outside the door. The northwest wind was blowing wildly, and the snow was falling harder, sprinkling on the face and body of the eldest nephew, who was stuck in the snow, like the tip of a mustard green peeking out of the garden.

Xiu Zhen stood there like a wooden chicken. At this time, her mother came back with a sheng of millet. When she saw her grandson lying in the snow, she quickly picked him up and brought him in. The millet was scattered all over the ground in the panic. She supported the child, picking up the rice one grain at a time, muttering:

"Being so impatient, even if you want to hit the child, you can only gently slap his buttocks a few times to scare him; you can't throw him in the snow like that! If the child gets sick from the cold, won't you be anxious again?"

After all, he was her own son. Her sister-in-law took a towel to wipe away the tears and snow from her eldest son.

"Isn't it true, what you scatter, you reap." The mother said.

The sister-in-law got angry, and she immediately twitched her lips:

"I want to hit him, I want to love him, he's my own son, who dares to talk to me? You know how to raise children, you know how to teach children, why didn't you raise a good son?"

"Where did I raise a bad son! Look! I want to ask you!"

"Not bringing back a single penny, not even a letter, this is your son! Such a son, is that what you raised?" The sister-in-law said, taking a step with each sentence, pointing her finger at her mother's nose.

"My son is like this, it's not my fault, it's your bad luck! Why isn't your luck a little better? Then your husband would earn money for you to use."

"It's my fault? You old hag's bad luck has covered up your son's good luck. It's your old life that's bad!"

The mother was so angry that she couldn't say a word, her lips trembling, her hands stretched out, wanting to tear her daughter-in-law's mouth, if Xiu Zhen hadn't stepped forward to dissuade her, they would have almost started a fight. If they had started a fight, of course, the mother would have suffered.

The sister-in-law's anger had not subsided, and she continued to scold:

Legal Advice 173

(Question)

(1) My grandparents gave birth to my father and my uncle. They separated long ago. My grandfather died early. My grandmother is still healthy. My parents have no children, so they adopted me as their daughter because I am his niece and have blood relations. They plan to give me all the property and inheritance rights. Is this legally permissible? What kind of procedures should be followed?

(2) My uncle also had no children. My uncle also died. He adopted a nephew to inherit for both him and his wife. He had already given the customary "filial piety" payments. But after my aunt dies, can the remaining property belong to me?

(3) My grandmother also mentioned the property for living expenses. Because she is old, her livelihood is entirely provided by my family, and she has agreed to give me all of her possessions. What procedures should be followed?

(4) The reason why my parents did not adopt a nephew as their son is because their knowledge is very limited and, moreover, they are from a distant clan. If my parents die, and they want to argue, how should I resist? (Asked by Pin Fang)

(Answer)

(1) If the lady has been adopted by her aunt and uncle since childhood, or if a contract was signed at the time of adoption, then when the inheritance begins in the future, she can inherit the adoptive parents' estate according to law, without the need for other procedures.

(2) No.

(3) This is an act of donation. A donation occurs when one party expresses the intention to give his own property to the other party without compensation, and the donation becomes effective upon acceptance by the other party (see Article 406 of the Civil Code). However, if the donation involves property that cannot be transferred without registration (such as the transfer of real estate rights, which must be registered before it can be asserted against a third party), the donation does not take effect until the transfer registration has been completed (see Article 407 of the same law). Since the intentions expressed between the donor (your grandmother) and the donee (the lady) are consistent, in addition to paying attention to real estate registration, the donation is effective. It is also acceptable to draw up a written document if desired.

(4) The current law abolishes patriarchal inheritance. Unless the lady's adoptive parents voluntarily adopt a son from a distant clan, in the future, the son from a distant clan cannot claim inheritance based on patriarchal succession. If disputes arise in the future, the lady can defend herself according to the law.

Answered by Lawyer Pu Shunqing (Correspondence address: No. 4, Yiyu Fang, Lafayette Road, Shanghai)

Shen Bao Amateur Weekly

Amateur Ramblings

The Issue of the Existence of Rickshaws 174

— Shi Yong

Not long ago, the Shanghai Public Concession had a plan to improve municipal transportation, saying that it would gradually reduce the number of rickshaws in stages within a few years, first reducing them by a few tens of percent, gradually making them disappear, to facilitate traffic, reduce city noise, and increase people's happiness. The reverse of reducing rickshaws is to promote the use of automobiles, using machines instead of human labor. If one day, we are fortunate enough to be able to climb to the position of the automobile class, it will truly be a feeling of "what good fortune for the common people to be born in a prosperous age"!

In the 20th century, advocating science and using machines, of course, no one with a brain would disagree. Using the fruits of science is to increase the happiness of life, which is an easy theorem to prove, and we also hope that there will be such a day when all the happiness derived from the science girl can be commonly enjoyed by the general public. For example, take electricity, not only can wealthy families install electric lights and radios, but also in slums and remote areas there is brilliant electric light flickering and pleasant music permeating, making the entire space bright and surrounding the entire earth with songs of happiness. Similarly, we also hope that one day everyone will have a Ford car. Not only will they no longer have to labor their jade toes, but they will also be able to save time. Let us imagine how happy this world will be!

Therefore, in this regard, the good intentions of the Public Concession authorities are worthy of gratitude. But the science girl always has an arrogant temper and snobbish eyes. She will only lower her voice and serve obediently among princes, nobles, and ladies. When she encounters poor people, not only is it impossible to get close to her, but she is often subjected to her meanness and bullying. When a 1936 Ford car whizzes past in front of us, the scientific happiness we enjoy is a nose full of dust and smoke. For example, in my hometown, when villagers want to go to the city, they originally relied on rickshaws costing four cents per trip. One year, a gasoline boat company was opened, completely seizing all the rickshaw business. Rickshaw pullers, faced with hunger and cold, sold their human power as cheaply as machine power. That is to say, the fare for taking a gasoline boat was two cents, and the rickshaw was also only two cents. In this way, under the rickshaw pullers' desperate struggle against the machine, they were able to temporarily survive by relying on the leftovers of science. However, most of the rickshaw pullers were finally squeezed into the ranks of the unemployed.

We cannot deny that many tragedies will inevitably occur on the road from human power to science, but what methods will we use to avoid the cruelty of science? This is a problem worth studying.

The large number of rickshaws in Shanghai does hinder traffic, and the noisy city sounds do annoy the noble people in the ten-mile foreign concession. However, we have to think about why there are so many rickshaws? Why are rickshaw pullers willing to do this most laborious and lowly life like cattle and horses? Here, we encounter a serious social problem. Economic panic, industrial and commercial decline, and increased unemployment are a series of facts that we cannot close our eyes and simply dismiss. We support advocating science, so we also support abolishing rickshaws (but not like some philanthropists who do not sit in rickshaws for humanitarian reasons), but at the same time, we firmly advocate that in order to abolish rickshaws, the livelihood problems of tens of thousands of rickshaw pullers and their families should be properly and even fundamentally resolved.

Not long after the Public Concession announced its new policy plan, the French Concession registered rickshaws, and an alarming tragedy occurred in which dozens of rickshaw pullers were injured when they were arrested beyond the boundary. Is it really impossible for the fate of rickshaw pullers to escape the cruel slaughter of science? Alas!

The Confession of a Professional Woman

Royal Woman 175

— Miss Bai Hong Speaks

When I was a child, I loved to hum songs in a babbling voice. Therefore, being immersed in singing and dancing all day long as I am now, I find it to be a career that suits my personality quite well, although I haven't achieved much in singing and dancing.

I remember starting to step into the realm of singing and dancing in the spring of six years ago, when I was just thirteen years old. Generally speaking, a girl of that age would never have the opportunity to leave her family to pursue her hobbies. However, unexpectedly, I did so, and even broke free from the old family with its very strong feudal consciousness. This can truly be considered a miracle in my short life history, no wonder I still don't want to forget it!

In these six long years, I haven't fully learned everything I wanted to learn, which is a bit of a disappointment. However, I have since embarked on a journey of self-sufficiency in life, which is somewhat comforting.

Speaking of my family situation, I simply don't want to think about it, although they don't have any ill feelings towards me. Therefore, since I came to Shanghai, the impression of my family seems to have gradually faded away with the passing of time. Now I only remember that I am a banner-man belonging to the Plain Yellow Banner (a branch of the Manchu Qing imperial family). Relying on the military achievements of our ancestors in conquering the Han people, our branch was able to enjoy the preferential treatment of aristocratic life. However, I don't know from which generation of ancestors we moved from the vast deserts of Mongolian yurts to Peiping (Beijing).

It is said that at that time, the life of a group of imperial relatives—including my family, of course—was very decadent and boring. They were simply idle all day long, or rather, they had nothing to do. They only pursued their individual hobbies: strolling through the hutongs (alleys), raising birds, cockfighting, horse racing. The older ones would grow flowers at home, play chess, or invite two or three peers to tea houses to enjoy tea and wine, or go to bookstores to listen to storytellers or to opera houses to listen to operas. Endless time was spent on these activities until they died. However, subsequent generations would still inherit the legacy of their ancestors and continue their efforts. Thus, until the end of the Qing Dynasty, their way of life only changed somewhat with the ruthless environment.

My father was also a typical figure among these imperial relatives, with a mind full of feudal consciousness.

Page 20

Everything new, in his eyes, was as terrible as floods and fierce beasts. Although he didn't prevent me from entering the world of singing and dancing, this was only because an unfortunate fate dominated his consciousness. Otherwise, perhaps I would still be "living in seclusion in the boudoir"! However, the success of a thing sometimes requires the coincidence of objective circumstances. For example, if our family hadn't "declined," my father's thinking would never have changed. Furthermore, without my mother's encouragement, he would never have been willing to put down his dignified face and voluntarily let me engage in singing and dancing. Moreover, if the Bright Moon Song and Dance Troupe hadn't traveled to Peiping at that time, even if I wanted to engage in singing and dancing, I would have "no way to enter."

In Peiping, those who registered to join the Bright Moon Troupe at the same time as me included Li Mingjian and Ying Yin. Except for Ying Yin, who was a bit older, the rest were girls of eleven or twelve years old. Now Ying Yin has left the Bright Moon Troupe and has her own future, but Li Mingjian and I continue to be together, loving each other. We both believe that singing and dancing is a lifelong career, and hope that the Bright Moon Troupe can be carried forward and developed by us, if it doesn't encounter unexpected setbacks. After we, a group of children, joined in Peiping, we soon followed this "circus-like" group and left Peiping for Qingdao. We performed once in Qingdao, where I made my "virgin" debut. However, because it wasn't an important role, it didn't attract people's attention at the time. After staying in Qingdao for a short time, this large group of people marched grandly to Shanghai. From that time on, we began a period of learning on the right track.

Mr. Li Jinhui placed great hope on us new members who joined in Peiping. Therefore, he personally taught almost all the dances. When teaching members to learn singing and dancing, his attitude was very strict, putting on the face of a moralist, like a private tutor supervising the members to practice their lessons. Xu Lai, the first female member of the Bright Moon Troupe, was able to enjoy such a great reputation in the modern film industry because she was greatly influenced by him. He paid attention to the members' lives as if they were his own children. He recognized Li Mingjian as his goddaughter because he was afraid that she would feel lonely and uncomfortable in her life.

The first step of my lesson when I first entered the Bright Moon Troupe was to learn simple singing. I hummed all day long, and no one forbade me from doing so. Six months later, I began to learn basic dance steps. The instructor—Mr. Jinhui—always watched by the side, and if there was anything wrong, he would come forward to correct it, and he would also make some gestures himself. This lesson seemed a little more difficult than singing at the time. The reason was that I was used to singing in school, but I didn't have many opportunities to learn dancing. Therefore, when I came here to start learning dancing, my steps naturally seemed stiff. In addition, the instructor supervised me closely, which further increased the panic of my movements. After suffering for several days—at least, that's what I thought at the time—the surrounding environment seemed different. Everything became familiar, and the feeling of timidity disappeared. From then on, whenever a new dance came out, I would understand it as soon as I was instructed once or twice.

Cultivating a new talent is similar to a stonemason carving a utensil. The craftsman must have advanced skills to express his art, but the material must also be able to withstand the craftsman's carving. Learning singing and dancing is like that. It seems easy and shallow, but it's not easy to teach or learn. I have been learning here for more than a year, but I still dare not believe how much I have learned, although I am already studying acting skills and opera theory.

The Bright Moon Troupe was led by Mr. Li before, and he is still leading it now. However, now there are several more instructors, such as Mr. Li Jinguang, so the internal organization and management are more scientific than before. However, what's worth mentioning here is that the finances of the troupe are public, and the life is disciplined. The members should fulfill their pure obligations to the troupe, and at the same time have absolute rights. For example, we were taught by Mr. Li, and now we must fulfill the same obligations to the members who joined later, because in this way, the troupe can reduce the expense of hiring teachers. Now there are more than thirty new and old members here, and the monthly regular expenses are several hundred yuan. Our group is not a capital combination, and it has no economic background. To maintain the growth of this group, we can only rely on everyone's income from external performances to subsidize the troupe's expenses. Therefore, we only have life here, not remuneration. The members' food and accommodation are provided by the troupe, and the money transferred by the members—such as the income from radio broadcasting—is also counted as the troupe's income. If there is a little surplus in monthly expenses, everyone can share the money. For example, last time at the New Light performance of "Peanuts," each person got more than three yuan.

Our life as members here is a bit like a military life—no, it's simply military discipline. Isn't that right? In times of national crisis, soldiers sometimes have no pay to take and have to fight on the battlefield. When the singing scene is silent, we are the same. We have no money to take and still have to work hard for singing and dancing. Getting up at five o'clock in the morning to practice singing is not the same as soldiers getting up at dawn to drill? We practice from five o'clock to eight o'clock before eating breakfast. We have classes from nine o'clock until twelve o'clock for lunch, with only half an hour of rest in between. In the afternoon, we "cook in the same way" from one o'clock to five o'clock. At nine o'clock in the evening, the lights are turned off, and we get a longer rest. However, those who have to broadcast on the radio are an exception.

My life experience is not very rich, so if I want to say something, it seems that there is nothing worth saying. However, in the six years that I have stepped into the world of singing and dancing, I have followed the Bright Moon Troupe to Nanjing, Hankou, Qingdao, Wuxi, Suzhou, and other places for performances, living a nomadic life. I have received many good criticisms, and I have also been subjected to many sarcastic satires. These personal slanders are what a person engaged in art should encounter, and it is not worth worrying about. However, the Chinese singing and dancing scene has struggled for more than ten years, and it can only attract the attention of three or four critics (?), which makes me feel inexplicably disappointed! Like last time when we performed at the New Light Theater, those critics who claimed to be the vanguard of the times said that we were acting like clowns, using this superficial perspective to interpret singing and dancing, it really makes us in the singing and dancing scene want to cry out loud!

Current Affairs Research

The Naval Question in Europe 176

— Ke Cheng

Germany's declaration to rearm not only makes France and Italy feel uneasy, but even Britain, which is known as the king of the seas, feels that the situation is not good. Because, as it stands, the result of Germany's rearmament is that its air force will inevitably surpass Britain's, which goes without saying. At the same time, even Britain's traditional so-called two-power standard will be in danger of not being preserved. Therefore, after Germany declared its rearmament, Britain had to think more about the naval question and quickly come up with appropriate countermeasures.

Originally, since the Napoleonic Wars, Britain, which had mastered the world's hegemony, had adopted the two-power standard at the end of the nineteenth century, that is, Britain must maintain the naval power jointly possessed by the two largest naval powers in the world. In April 1898, Germany engaged in major naval construction, and then greatly expanded it. By 1909, Germany's naval power was almost equal to Britain's. At that time, Baldwin, the leader of the British Conservative Party in opposition, said in Parliament that the British Navy had long lost its two-power standard qualification. Immediately, Britain abandoned the two-power standard and recognized the 16:10 British-German naval ratio. This was the first blow that the British Navy's two-power standard encountered. Later, as a result of the World War, the German Navy was completely destroyed, and Britain celebrated its long-term consolidation of its maritime hegemony. But unfortunately, American power developed during the war, and it actively expanded its navy with its huge financial resources, causing Britain to feel the pain of being unable to compete with it. So, at the Washington Conference, Britain finally recognized the condition of equal British and American navies. But in Europe, Britain still maintained the two-power standard, that is, Britain still had the naval power jointly possessed by the two largest naval powers in Europe, France and Italy. Now that Germany has declared its rearmament, it will inevitably continue to compete with the major powers in expanding its armaments. Seeing this, in order to preserve its two-power standard in Europe, Britain quickly conducted naval negotiations with Germany, and the result was the establishment of the Anglo-German Naval Agreement.

The Anglo-German Naval Agreement stipulates that the German Navy will always maintain 35% of the British Navy's power. In this way, Germany has actually abolished the military clauses in the Treaty of Versailles and obtained the right to rearm. At the same time, Britain has also obtained a ratio that will always give it an advantage over Germany in naval matters, and it has maintained the balance of power between France, Germany, and Italy, that is, it has maintained the British Navy's two-power standard in Europe. Therefore, when the news of the Anglo-German Naval Agreement came out, London and Berlin both unanimously proclaimed the victory of their policies. But France and Italy were not very happy about this. Politicians in Paris unanimously declared that the Anglo-German Naval Agreement was a violation of the Treaty of Versailles and the London Declaration of March 2nd. This atmosphere of opposition to the Anglo-German Naval Agreement is still maintained today.

The Washington Conference also decided that the French and Italian naval ratio to the British and American should be 35%. Although the French actively opposed this decision, the combined naval power of France and Italy has still failed to exceed that of Britain. Currently, France's naval power is 560,000 tons, while Italy's is only 370,000 tons. According to the provisions of the Treaty of Versailles, the total tonnage of the German Navy can only be more than 150,000 tons. But after the Anglo-German Naval Agreement was established, the German Navy could increase to 420,000 tons, and it could immediately build 300,000 tons of new-style warships. In this way, Germany's naval power would be equal to France's. Compared to Italy, it has a great advantage. From this, it can be seen that France and Italy's opposition to the Anglo-German Naval Agreement has a major reason. Judging from the current situation, the naval question in Europe will cause more disputes due to the Anglo-German Naval Agreement. In this dispute, the major powers will inevitably compete to expand their navies and enter the most dangerous situation. In fact, France and Italy have formally stated that they will not necessarily abide by the 35% ratio to Britain and the United States stipulated in the Washington Treaty. The trend of the major powers competing to expand their navies has already been clearly revealed.

At the same time, although France and Italy have a certain degree of consensus on opposing the Anglo-German Naval Agreement, they still have major conflicts on the naval question. In fact, Italy insists on the view that the French and Italian navies should be equal. The reason is that Italy has a larger population than France, its coastline is also longer than France's, and its important metropolises are all close to the coast, so a strong navy is needed to defend them. At the same time, France can transport the iron, coal, oil, and other materials it needs by land, while Italy must rely on overseas supply, so Italy's navy must be equal to France's. However, in France's view, France is the second largest country in the world with vast colonies, and its country is also adjacent to the North Sea, the Atlantic Ocean, and the Mediterranean Sea. All coastal areas are in danger of being attacked by enemy fleets. Moreover, in the event of an emergency, France must also recruit black troops from Africa. Therefore, France resolutely opposes the French and Italian navies being equal. In the past, at the Washington Conference, there were many disputes over the question of French and Italian naval equality. This dispute is still continuing, and in the upcoming disarmament conference and naval conference, this question of equality will also be one of the problems that cannot be solved.

At the time of the Washington Conference, the main disputes in Europe were only between Britain, France, and Italy. Germany was not yet prepared to rearm at that time. In the disputes over the naval question in Europe, Germany can be said to have been an outsider. But just the many disputes between Britain, France, and Italy were enough to give European politicians a headache. As already mentioned, Britain's so-called two-power standard, Italy's claim to be equal to France, and France's anti-British and anti-Italian views are in conflict with each other. It is in this mutual conflict that European politicians have exhausted their efforts and schemed against each other, but they have not been able to solve the naval question in Europe at all. They have only made the disputes more and more numerous and the situation more and more serious! Now, Germany has resolutely declared its rearmament, and the Anglo-German Naval Agreement has been established. Needless to say, Germany will inevitably become one of the main disputants in the European naval question in the future, and the problem will become more complex and more serious, which we can also assert.

Literary Works

Before the Watchtower 177

— Shao Han

A good moon—just showing half its face in the east, and the earth already felt brighter. Her beautiful, clear gaze shifted to the north of the chimney, looking askance at the Zhangde railway station; everything there, moving, still, joyful, sorrowful, was all reflected in her eyes.

Well-fed and well-clothed people, in their own courtyards and on the watchtowers, arranged incense, flowers, and fruits to welcome the New Year, a time for new clothes. In an instant, the lights and candles shone brightly, and firecrackers resounded through the sky, thus completing the welcoming ceremony. A moment later, the scene changed again: on a vermilion round table were displayed fresh tea and snacks, and a sumptuous feast was spread out. At the family's peaceful gathering, the adults were very relaxed, and the children's faces were filled with boundless joy. As they raised their glasses to the bright moon, they felt that life was beautiful and the family was sweet. But under the same bright moonlight, in the same atmosphere of joy, another tragedy was about to unfold.

Next to the platform, there was a small inn—Fatty's Inn. Half a month ago, a young couple came, their names on the register were: "Li Er, Wang Liujie." They were not merchants, officials, nor wandering vagabonds. Their actions were vulgar, and their speech was full of rustic flavor. After checking in, they had no relatives visiting, no friends to look after them. In this bustling world, they were all alone!

Over the past ten days or so, Liujie always wore a sorrowful face, huddled in the pigeon coop-like side room, quietly shedding tears and sighing softly! Li Er seemed to be avoiding a disaster, leaving the inn early every day, sometimes not returning wearily until dusk. Today, he left early again, and his shadow is still nowhere to be seen!

Liujie sat alone on the wooden bed, staring blankly with dull eyes at the dim kerosene lamp. She seemed to be in a daze, or perhaps she had lost consciousness. When the sound of firecrackers outside entered the secluded side room, she finally seemed to come to her senses and turned her head. In an instant, firecrackers went off one after another, as if unable to restrain emotional impulses. She hysterically went to the door and lifted the bamboo curtain to look out. At this moment, the moonlight was exceptionally bright, and there was not a single cloud in the sky. It was truly a beautiful night. Later, the sound of firecrackers gradually became hoarse, monotonous, and finally faded away with two or one crack at a time.

The earth was quiet, with only the children's songs in the distance causing a slight ripple in the still air. But the song seemed contagious, and soon the nearby children joined in, so that every word and every line was clearly transmitted into Liujie's ears:

"The moon is bright, the moon is round,

The whole family gathers around.

Little sister eats mooncakes,

Little brother learns to play finger-guessing games.

Poor Aunt Wang next door,

Her husband left and never returned!"

This ordinary song, this childish, nonsense song, actually stirred Liujie's heartstrings, evoking her memories of tragic past events.

She remembered that before the Lunar New Year, due to the pressure of rent and debts, and the scourge of life, she finally had to sever the love between mother and child. She exchanged her own five-year-old son, Xiao Niu Zi, for fifty silver dollars from Widow Sun! After paying the rent and debts, there were still twenty dollars left. The couple held this sorrowful sum and still toiled in the fields, playing with mud in the starlight and moonlight. Sometimes they looked at the Guan Wang deity statue covered with dust on the wall, hoping that the god of the fields would give them a better harvest, hoping that the land would repay all their losses. However, as time turned to May and June of this year, the heavens did not send a drop of rain to the ground. The wheat ears were withering, and the corn was turning yellow. The couple's blood and sweat were still in vain, and all hope

Page 21

disappeared like bubbles. When it came time to pay the rent in July, there was no harvest in the fields, and no food left in the house. The money from selling the son was already spent, and there were no more sons to sell! But what about Zhang the landlord's rent and the couple's future life? In the end, they had no choice but to flee their ancestral home and run to Zhangde, hundreds of miles away...

The tragic past was already tightly bound to Liujie's heart. Moreover, during this Mid-Autumn Festival, seeing the reunions of other families and hearing the lively songs of other children, further stirred up her feelings of longing for her son and her home. She could not help but feel sore all over and collapsed softly on the bed.

As she was about to drift into a dream in a daze, the door panel suddenly creaked open. She raised her head alertly and realized it was her husband. She struggled to move her stiff body and went to his side: "Why are you back so late?"

He did not answer, but sat wearily on the lame stool. His melancholy face and abnormal expression greatly surprised her.

"How was today?"

"Nothing," Li Er said, forcing himself to remain calm, and then took out four mooncakes from his pocket, handing three to her, "Today is the Mid-Autumn Festival..." His voice was very choked and finally stopped.

Liujie held the mooncakes, as if losing consciousness, staring blankly at her husband, without saying a word.

After a long silence, Li Er gently walked to Liujie's side, put his left hand on her shoulder, and pressed his right hand against his chest.

"Liujie, we, husband and wife..." He sobbed nervously, his moist eyes emitting a terrifying light.

Liujie stood up abruptly and asked in surprise, "What's wrong? What's wrong with you today..."

Li Er hesitated for a while and finally said painfully, "Liujie, I'm leaving tonight..." He took out a paper package from his pocket, "These three dollars, keep them safe."

"Where to..."

"Baoding. —Today I ran to the mine and waited all day, but still no hope. Several people were laid off the day before yesterday, and I think there's no point in waiting any longer." Li Er took a long breath, "I thought, sooner or later I'll die anyway, so on the way back I ran into recruiters, and I signed up..."

"Are you really going? I..." Liujie suddenly cried out "Wah" and tightly gripped his collar with both hands.

Li Er was at a loss, tearing off a piece of his ragged shirt to wipe her tears, while tears were also rolling down his own face: "Don't cry! What can we do? Are we just going to starve to death! Think about it, we've been here in Zhangde for almost twenty days, looking for work every day, at the coal mines, flour mills, and cargo yards, we've waited everywhere. But..."

Liujie was now a little more sober, thinking that her husband's words were indeed correct: when the two of them fled to Zhangde, they thought that there were railways, coal mines, and flour mills here, and as long as they were not lazy, they would definitely find work; who knew that one day, two days, until now, they were still both idle; seeing that their clothes were all sold, and they owed a lot of money to the inn, were they really going to starve to death together? Thinking of this, she sympathized with him and forgave him. But he was leaving so simply, leaving her behind, how would she end up? So she felt very sad again and burst into tears: "You're leaving, but I... what will happen to me...?"

Li Er's attitude was very awkward, and he felt as if countless needles were pricking his heart. After a long, long time, he burst out with a painful voice: "You?... I've already discussed it with Old Fatty, he can take care of you..."

Liujie had just opened her mouth when a strange call suddenly rang out outside the door: "Li Er." Immediately, the door curtain was lifted, and a man in military uniform appeared. He glanced at Liujie and then said to Li Er, "The '72' train leaves at 12:15, make sure to be there."

"Yes." Li Er responded mechanically.

Immediately, there was a burst of miserable crying in the room!

The hands of the clock at the station were about to point to "XII". A round, bright moon hung in the center of the sky; there was not a trace of dust in the universe, and all the secrets on the earth were exposed in the clear waves of light. At this moment, a man and a woman were standing at the entrance of Fatty's Inn; in the cold moonlight, the man's face was particularly pale, and his whole body was trembling as if in spasm. The woman leaned slightly on him, as if she had lost consciousness, her face was green, and her body was limp. They stood like this for five minutes. The bell at the station rang, and the whistle emitted its first cry. The man suddenly became alert, suddenly pushing the woman away. His mouth opened and closed, and his chest rose and fell, as if he wanted to speak, or as if he was breathing. His eyes stared sluggishly at her, not knowing whether it was love or hate. At this moment, a middle-aged fatty stood at the low doorway, his hands on his hips, his head swaying, as if he was watching something interesting. The man suddenly turned to the fatty and said pleadingly, "Boss, please take good care of her, don't sell her..."

"Don't worry." The fatty's voice was unusually gentle, "Go, go quickly!"

"Woo! Woo!..." The train let out a long, mournful cry, and all that could be seen at the station was people crowding around. The man suddenly hugged the woman and spat out a hoarse voice:

"Liujie..." He choked with sobs and could not utter a word, only looking at the round moon in the sky with both eyes.

"Ding-dong, ding-dong!" The last bell was ringing at the station. He suddenly broke free from the woman's hands and ran madly towards the station. She staggered after him, but fell to the ground with a "wah" after only three steps!

At this moment, someone on the watchtower of the coal mine company opposite was enjoying the moon with a prostitute. Amidst the excited music, a girl hummed a line from Pinggui Biedong: "It made us... husband and wife... part..."

Overseas Correspondence Network

Coffee Country 178

— Yi

Correspondence from Santos, Brazil

Brazil is a country in South America that is rich in resources and vast in area. England, the United States, and other countries have huge investments here. Therefore, although Brazil is still nominally an independent country, in reality, its politics and economy are dominated by England, the United States, and other countries. There are four kinds of residents here: the Indians who lived here before Columbus discovered America, the Europeans who migrated later, the African blacks who were imported by the Europeans as labor, and the mixed-blood hybrids. Now, except for the uncivilized Indians living in remote areas, these different races are unified under one government, one language, and one religion (Brazil is a Catholic country). Therefore, it is very difficult to clearly point out its unique national character; however, if you pay attention to observation, you can see the customs and human sentiments of the so-called Brazilians in many places.

First of all, it is worth noting the Brazilians' hospitality towards their guests and visitors. If you visit Brazilians, they will make every effort to find out what you like, and then try their best to make you feel comfortable and happy in all aspects. A Frenchman who had been to South America once said: "We were very welcomed in Argentina, Chile, and Peru, but the treatment we received in Brazil was better than anywhere else, it was just like being in our own home."

Brazilians are very passionate. Not only in the love between men and women, but also in the friendship between general same-sex friends, their passionate emotional expressions are somewhat unusual. In Brazil, if two friends who have been separated for two weeks meet again, the surprise and cordiality they express emotionally will exceed that of friends in other places who have been separated for ten years; they will not only shake hands enthusiastically, but also hug and cheer. In the streets here, you can often see two men embracing each other frantically, but they are just ordinary friends who have only been separated for two weeks, not people with deep relationships who have not seen each other for many years. Someone said, "The character of Brazilians is gentle and kind, but also terrifyingly rough": this is indeed a fair comment in some respects.

Brazilians also love Brazil's natural beauty and undeveloped resources: the first Brazilians are eager for their country to develop day by day, to use their own strength to develop its resources, and to make their country occupy a superior position in the world. But—under the control of the political and economic forces of England, the United States, and other countries, their hopes will not become a reality unless there is a major change in the fundamentals. In recent years, due to the stimulation of objective facts, some more progressive Brazilians have also seen this point, so they have gradually become less "hospitable" to England, the United States, and other countries.

However, generally speaking, because Brazil is rich in special products and easy to live in, the general temperament of Brazilians is more lazy and lacks the will to work hard, struggle, and make progress. The average Brazilian always postpones things that can be done today until tomorrow or even the day after tomorrow. There are few great achievers in Brazil, and the main reason is of course that Brazil's culture is backward, and that the aggression of British, American, and other imperialisms has hindered its development, but the lazy bad habits of its people are also related.

Compared to its vast land, Brazil is a sparsely populated country. However, due to the development of capitalism, there are also very large cities in Brazil, and their degree of prosperity is no less than that of cities in Europe and the United States. Rio de Janeiro has a population of two million, and Sao Paulo also has a population of more than one million. In such large cities, as in large cities in Europe and the United States, there are radio broadcasts, large airships flying in the sky, more than thirty-story Western-style buildings, groups of cars, movies, music, and of course, modern men and women, as well as Pekingese dogs.

Driving north from Sao Paulo, after a while, the urban atmosphere of Brazil disappears: on both sides of the car are vast coffee plantations; the houses that appear in front of you are not modern buildings of more than thirty stories, but crude bungalows; there are many cattle-herding men on the grasslands, most of whom have dozens of cows around them. Once you arrive at the station, it's even more interesting. Here you can see many mixed-race, half-black girls riding on mules and horses, specially to greet their husbands; when she gets off the mule and horse and receives her husband who is coming down from the train, she must embrace him in a passionate and long embrace as if she were crazy. When the train stops or starts in such places, it does not sound the whistle as a signal, but rings a bell: when the bell rings for the train to stop and the train stops at a station, in addition to coming down one after another to watch the scenery of these places, many passengers will take the opportunity to drink a cup of extremely black and strong coffee.

If you go from a large city in Brazil to the countryside, you will be surprised to feel that you have arrived in another world. Because the countryside here not only lacks tall buildings, and not only is the material equipment very different from the cities, but also the social relations and living conditions are one or two centuries behind the cities. The villagers in Brazil mainly grow coffee in the countryside, but the owners of the coffee lands are feudal-era lords. Therefore, although Brazil's cities have been modernized, its countryside is still stuck in the feudal era. In such a rural area, of course, the feudal landlords dominate everything, and so-called law and justice have no meaning here, and the general public does not know these things; all that is recognized is the authority of God and the feudal landlords.

Brazilians like to dance, and they start dancing whenever they are tired from farming. Sometimes they play pleasant music and dance wildly. They are even more happy when foreigners go there to play music. During the dance, the women here often love to drape the beautiful fabrics they get from the Turks over their heads and dance wildly with the young men, sometimes even indulging in dancing all night without sleeping, until dawn, when the parrots sing and the cows moo, then they end their frenzied dancing.

Gambling and alcohol are also particularly loved by Brazilians. Whether on the streets or in general squares, you can see Brazilians gambling; in addition, there are many large casinos here, and their architecture and facilities are very luxurious. As for their love of alcohol, it is proportional to their love of gambling. They can go a day without eating bread, but they cannot go a day without drinking alcohol. The alcohol they drink is mostly a strong shochu made from sugarcane, which seems somewhat inconsistent with their warm temperament, but in fact it is so. However, the good thing about Brazilians who like alcohol is that they are different from American, Russian, and even Chinese drunkards. After they get drunk, they quietly go to sleep, without causing trouble, without looking for someone to fight, without shouting and making noise in the streets, and without going crazy.

The Brazilian government also runs lotteries. There are generally two types: one is a small lottery once a week; spending one or two yuan to buy a lottery ticket gives you the hope of winning ten thousand or twenty thousand yuan; the other is an annual lottery, buying a lottery ticket for one hundred yuan gives you the hope of winning six or seven hundred thousand yuan. Brazilians' love of buying lottery tickets is no less than their love of gambling and drinking. Almost every Brazilian is a regular buyer of lottery tickets. Whether they are going out for a walk, meeting friends, or drinking coffee, Brazilians will not forget to buy a lottery ticket to take home.

Special Account

Overseas Chinese in the World (6) 179

— Zhong Minyi

During the mid-Ming Dynasty, the Spanish occupied the Philippines. Subsequently, they greatly oppressed the overseas Chinese in the Philippines. In 1603, a conflict in Manila between Chinese and Spaniards resulted in the deaths of as many as 23,000 Chinese. In 1638, the Spanish killed another 33,000 overseas Chinese. In 1660, after Zheng Chenggong (Koxinga) took Taiwan, overseas Chinese seized the opportunity to revolt. After the failure of the revolt, almost all were brutally massacred by the Spanish. When the Philippines came under American control, the American government strictly prohibited Chinese laborers from coming to the Philippines. Therefore, although China and the Philippines have deep ties, the number of overseas Chinese in the Philippines is not as large as in Siam (Thailand) and Vietnam. If not for the failure of the Philippine revolution against Spain in the early 19th century, when the Spanish devoted all their efforts to suppressing the Filipinos, allowing the Chinese to take the opportunity to come to the Philippines in droves, perhaps there would be no Chinese presence in the Philippines at all. But even today, the total number of overseas Chinese in the Philippines is only around 100,000.

However, overseas Chinese in the Philippines hold a significant position in industry and commerce. Industries such as cocoa, tobacco, ramie, coconuts, timber, textiles, and sugar are all deeply connected with overseas Chinese. According to an American government survey, there are thirty-one rice mills in central Luzon, of which twenty-eight are operated by overseas Chinese. Among the many Chinese merchants, we can name two of the most famous: Xu Gongping and Ye Tieke. The former trades in rice, hemp, and other commodities, owns ships, and has branches in major cities, with insurance, shipping, and banking departments within the company. The latter is an overseas Chinese who started as a worker. His Ye Tieke Company also mainly deals in agricultural products, with three large warehouses in Manila and six branches in other locations. Branches are also established in Hong Kong, Shanghai, Xiamen, Zhenjiang, Ningbo, and other places, with shipping, insurance, and banking departments internally as well. This not only shows the grand scale of the businesses run by Xu and Ye, but also how important a position overseas Chinese hold in the industry and commerce of the Philippines.

Overseas Chinese in the Philippines are also very active in cultural and educational undertakings. Here, there are not only many Chinese-run daily newspapers, but also various publications. In Manila, there are many schools established by overseas Chinese, and they are well-managed, so Chinese schools in various parts of Southeast Asia use them as models.

However, since the European War, overseas Chinese in the Philippines have suffered greatly from the maltreatment of the American government. For example, the shipping companies are prohibited from Chinese investment, rice prices are restricted, and the compulsory implementation of the European and American accounting regulations are all ruthless attacks on overseas Chinese. Recently, the Filipinos' call for "The Philippines for Filipinos" and the open rejection of overseas Chinese, coupled with the fierce competition from ×× people, have dealt a major blow to overseas Chinese in the Philippines.

Dutch East Indies

The Dutch East Indies, also known as the Dutch East Indies, is located in Southeast Asia, northwest of Australia, and is formed by a group of islands. Among the islands are five main islands: Java, Madura, Sumatra, Borneo, Celebes, and New Guinea. Besides these five major islands, there are many smaller islands, such as the Lesser Sunda Islands and the Moluccas. In total, the Dutch East Indies has an area of two million square kilometers, accounting for about half of all of Europe (excluding European Russia).

The time when Chinese people came to the Dutch East Indies was probably around the same time they arrived in other parts of Southeast Asia. However, the development of overseas Chinese here became more prominent after the Dutch occupied the East Indies in the early 17th century. Although the East Indies have abundant natural resources, their inhabitants are primitive and uncivilized. They are ignorant and stubborn, unable to develop the natural resources. Therefore, after the Dutch arrived, in order to develop the natural resources, they devised ways to attract hardworking and enduring Chinese laborers to the islands.

In the areas of Hong Kong, Shantou, and Xiamen, the Dutch recruited large numbers of Chinese laborers to exploit mineral deposits. These laborers were called "contract laborers," meaning they were slaves of the Dutch, working for them for life, subject to their abuse, even to the point of death. Therefore, people from Guangdong called the Chinese laborers recruited by the Dutch "piglets." In addition, because the East Indies urgently needed a large amount of labor to develop mineral resources, the Dutch even resorted to extremely improper means, plundering Chinese people to work there.

Later, as the industry and commerce of the East Indies developed, many Chinese came here to open factories and run businesses. Therefore, even now, there are more than one million overseas Chinese in the Dutch East Indies.

The main industry in the Dutch East Indies is sugar production, which is almost entirely controlled by the Dutch and Malays. Chinese investment in various large enterprises here is relatively low; however, the Chinese hold a very important position in commerce. The export of native agricultural products and the import of European, American, and Japanese goods must all go through the hands of the Chinese. In the area of commerce here, the only ones who can compete with the Chinese are the Arabs.

In recent years, overseas Chinese in the East Indies, like overseas Chinese in other regions, have suffered many blows. Most obviously, Chinese people here must find a guarantor to open a shop and sell goods, and apply for approval from the local government before they can start business. After starting business, they must also pay income tax, business tax, sanitation tax, furniture tax, etc. every year. If they fail to pay on time, they will be arrested.

Movie News

"Hero of the Times" at the Night Garden 180

Yi Hua is a famous scenery company. Almost every movie has to allocate a large sum of money to build the scenery. It was like that in the past, and even more so now.

If you run into the Yi Hua company these two days, those who have been there will be confused about how Yi Hua changed its face, and those who have not been there will wonder how Yi Hua opened in a big garden. What is the reason? Because Yi Hua is building a large "Night Garden" scene these days.

The Night Garden is the scenery in "Hero of the Times." The area is really amazing. It is surrounded by lights, like a long snake winding around. When they are all turned on, the scene is magnificent beyond description, and in the garden, in addition to pavilions and towers, there is also a huge stage. The new actress Wen Qiu is performing "Si Lang Visits His Mother" on the stage. The gongs and drums are deafening. We think the scene of Jia Fei touring the Grand View Garden in "Dream of the Red Chamber" is probably just like this.

Only Yi Hua builds such a big scene, and only "Hero of the Times" has such a big scene.

Lianhua's Three Major Contributions to Children's Year 181

"With healthy children, there will be everything." Now at the beginning of Children's Year, Lianhua has decided to contribute three great children's films to the builders of the new China, the masters of the future: The first film is "Little Angel" directed by Wu Yonggang, which is about to be premiered at the Jincheng Grand Theater in Shanghai. It thoroughly explains how to create an ideal and healthy child in a social environment and feudal forces.

The second film is "Lost Lamb" which Cai Chusheng is about to start filming. It shows how some wandering children struggle desperately and fight hard in various difficult environments, raising a serious issue for the entire society. The decision of actors, in addition to Ge Zuo Zhi and Chen Su Juan, there is a new actor list.

The third film is "Childhood China" directed by Fei Mu, starring Jin Yan and Li Keng. As the name suggests, it shows how children train and use their own power to create a glimmer of dawn for the new China under the struggle for survival of the entire nation.
